F. EXPECTEDBENEFITS

Besides the expected positive effects of the policy measures to be supported, the proposed
operation would have its impacts on state development through three additional channels: (i)
technical knowledge transfer, (ii) financial incentives to complete reforms, and (iii) promotion of
MGto investors by providing externalcredibility to the state's reforms and achievements so far. In
addition, the proposed operation would deliver significant benefits at the national level through
reinforcement of fiscal discipline in one of the largest states in the federation with troubled fiscal
performance in the recent past.

Knowledge transfer. Within certain areas there is scope for the Bank to advise the government on
technical aspects of policy design. Examples are the design of PPP contracts and regulatory
framework (e.g., in water and sanitation and in road transport), in systems of results-based
management, and in human resource management. All are areas where the Bank has technical
comparative ad~antage.~~

Financial incentives. Owing to the fiscal strictures the state faces, both tranches of the operation
would be relieving short-term liquidity constraints for the state government. As this would be an
untied budget support operation, the state government would have flexibility to determine how to
apply the loan resources. In principle, the state could use the additional liquidity for a variety of
purposes including (i) retiring highly burdensome debt taken on at costly terms, (ii) making certain
investments with high short-run returns for the government (e.g., modernization of tax collection),


35Brazil Country Assistance Strategy, 2003-2007, World Bank Report No. 27043-BR, December 2003, p. 33.
36During preparation, Bank staff and consultants have provided detailed input to the state government in
seven areas supported by the loan: (i)results-based public sector management; (ii) administrative reforms and
human resource management; (iii) strategic planning; (iv) fiscal sustainability analysis; (v) fiscal risk
mitigation in the state's civil service social security system; (vi) fiscal risk mitigation in the state's civil service
health insurance systems; and (vii) assessment of fiduciary systems.


                                                                                                                    31

(iii) funding its PPP guarantee fund to help promote growth, and (iv) planning for a prolonged
programof core high-returninvestments, particularly in infrastructure.

Promoting MG to investors by providing external credibility to state reform. Another
objective that has been emphasized by the state government i s the signaling role of World Bank
policy-based support at this stage, clearly associated with the government's program of structural
reforms, coming out of a difficult period of transition. To help promote Minas externally, there is
also the possibility of the World Bank Group's Foreign Investment Advisory Service (FIAS)
providing technical support to the state government.

National-levelbenefits. The proposed operation would also provide benefits at the national level.
These benefits can be divided into three broad categories: the demonstration effect of the World
Bank Group signaling support internationally for a high-performing state government;
strengthening an economy that together with Sgo Paul0 forms Brazil's "industrial engine"; and
reinforcing the Fiscal Responsibility Law by strengthening the fiscal adjustment process in a state
where public finances have until recently been precarious.

G. CHOICE OF INSTRUMENT

DPL versus investment lending. The operation supports policy reforms to which the state
government is highly committed. A DPL i s therefore the appropriate vehicle. As the section above
describes, the state's reform program is robust, and its overall development strategy, public
spending priorities, and financial management give firm grounds for confidence that the funds will
contribute to poverty reduction.

Two-tranche DPL versus programmatic lending. A series of programmatic DPLs would be an
ideal vehicle with which to support medium-term institutional reform agenda such as the one this
proposed loan would support in Minas Gerais. Unfortunately, Brazil's rigorous fiscal control
regime that has contributed so much to sustenance of fiscal responsibility since the late 1990s also
imposes relatively high transaction costs involved in processing sub-national loans. Each loan
would have to go through a rigorous process of multiple reviews and approvals by federal
government agencies, and often this approval process could take months or longer and introduces a
high degree of uncertainty regarding the timing of the loan approval. Given this reality, the MG
government has strongly preferred a two-tranche DPL for which a federal approval i s needed only
once, and the Bank concurred that under the circumstance a two-tranche DPL was the most
appropriate instrument.

DPL versus technical assistance. Another alternative would be TA lending focusing on areas
where the proposed operation would include TA in addition to policy-based lending. Given the
state's borrowing restrictions within its debt agreement with the federal government, the state has
not requested a separate TA loan, but instead intends to use a part of the proceeds of the operation
to fund consultancies in areas supported by the loan.

H. RELATIONSHIPTO OTHERBANK OPERATIONS

Existing World Bank Group support to Minas Gerais includes various activities: selective grant-
based funding; technical dialogue, both in the context of loan preparation and other recent
transactions; impact in the state through the execution of federal lending operations; and IFC
operations with the private sector. In addition, a state rural poverty reduction project has recently
become effective. The development of the proposed operation has benefited from the knowledge


                                                                                                 32

created by many of these activities, and its implementation would strengthen the enabling
environment for them all. Annex 11provides more detail on these other Bank operations.

As a first state-level DPL, the proposed operation also closely links with policy-based lending
support that the Bank has been providing Brazil over the past several years, especially in support of
the federal government's fiscal and competitiveness reform agenda. In recent years, the main
vehicles have been a series of three Programmatic Fiscal Reform Loans (January 2001-June 2004),
which have supported strengthening of fiscal management overall, including specific measures of
sub-national fiscal performance as a benchmark of fiscal sustainability of the country as a whole,
and the Programmatic Loan for Sustainable and Equitable Growth (January 2004), which
supported, inter alia, measures to improve national investment climates and infrastructure
provision, including the passage of the federal PPP Law. These programmatic series are still
ongoing, and are expected to generate positive synergy with the proposed operation that supports
relatedpolicy reforms at the state level.

I.COORDINATIONWITHOTHERDONORS

The main other internationallender involved in Minas Gerais is the IDB, which i s financing several
roads projects in the state. These projects, which include the improvement of road access between
Belo Horizonte and neighboringregions of the state, complement the presentproposed operation in
that they finance core infrastructure investments, while the Partnership for Development focuses on
the enabling policy and regulatory environment for sustainableeconomic growth in the state. IDB
has also offered grant-funded technical assistance to the PPP unit within the government, which
dovetails with the policy-based financial support to the PPP initiative and the design of the first
contracts. The Bank has had constructive and enriching dialogue with the IDB on the state's
framework for PPP.

Coordination with the IMF has taken place at the national level, and the Bank and the Fund
recently collaborated on the pilot initiative on public investment, with important effects interms of
strengthening the selection and appraisal of federal infrastructure projects. Again, particularly in
the area of transport infrastructure (principally roads), many of the benefits will be felt in time by
the state of Minas Gerais.

Finally, collaboration with the private sector has been intense via the Program for Excellence in
Public Management, which has drawn on private-sector funding of management consultants to
advise the government on cutting-edge management reforms in the areas of fiscal management,
hospital management, public security, and planning and administration. This has been an important
source of understanding for the Bank during loan preparation of the improvements to efficiency
that the government has achieved.

J. LESSONSLEARNED

The design of the proposed operation reflects several important lessons of recent experience with
DPLs in Braziland more broadly.

Most important is strong client ownership of the reform program being supported. This is assured
in the proposed operation by the close dialogue that the Bank has conducted with the State, and by
the approach taken whereby the government took a proactive role in defining policy matrix with
measures that were both high impact and feasible within the time frame of the operation.
Furthermore, the state government strongly supported the two-tranche design, as opposed to a


                                                                                                   33

single-tranche design, clearly cognizant of the implication that the release of the second tranche
would be conditional on their fulfilling the agreedconditions.

The second lesson is the need for strong leadership at the highest levels of government for
significant fiscal adjustment and deep public sector reforms to succeed. As attested to by a track
record of over two full years in government, the present state government benefits from the
necessary strength of leadership throughout the higher levels of government. This i s a key attribute
of the client that makes the proposed operation likely to succeed.

Further lessons are underlinedin the World Bank guidelines on sub-national policy-based lending.
Conditions for success that are listed include that the client be of significant magnitude to have an
impact at the national level.

A fourth lesson that we have learned from Brazil's repeatedeconomic crises in recent years is the
vital importance of economic growth in assuring fiscal sustainability. Fiscal adjustments that take
place against a background of recession or stagnation, and which in some cases may exacerbate
these problems, run into vicious cycles of declining revenues and the need for further belt-
tightening.    The proposed operation therefore pursues the dual goals of fiscal discipline and
economic growth intandem and with equal importance attachedto each.

A final lesson from Brazil i s the central role played by the Fiscal Responsibility Law in anchoring
the fiscal discipline at the consolidated national level within Brazil's system of fiscal federalism.
For this reason a strong principle of the design of the proposed operation i s to work within the
LRF,to support its implementation, and to further the achievementof the objectives set inthe debt
agreementsbetween the states and the federal government.

V.       OPERATIONIMPLEMENTATION

A. POVERTY AND SOCIAL IMPACTS

The main impacts of the operation on poverty will be through two channels: improved economic
growth and more efficient delivery of public services through improved management. It is not
possible to simulate realistically the disaggregated effects of the project on different socioeconomic
groups or geographical subdivisions of the state, however, since its effects will be felt statewide.

The benefits of the operation can be divided into various levels. At the first level, the operation
brings benefits in terms of reinforcing the Fiscal Responsibility Law and Brazil's system of fiscal
federal checks and balances. As discussed elsewhere in this document, this system has been
fundamental to assuring Brazil's national macroeconomic stability since the Real Plan, and by
reinforcing the successful adjustment of Brazil's second largest state, the operation has
considerable significance at the national level. As macroeconomic instability tends to exacerbate
poverty (especially in Brazil), maintenance of fiscal discipline, a basic requirement for
macroeconomic stability, i s an essential prerequisite for poverty reduction.

Second, within the state itself, the fiscal adjustment combined with improved economic
performance will lead to poverty reduction both through higher incomes and through increased
spending available for direct poverty-reducing spending, such as education, health, and basic local
infrastructure. Fiscal adjustments in Brazil have not tended to result inreduction in social spending
because at the federal level adjustments have been done by way of revenue increases. Social
expenditures in particular tend to be well-protected because of the constitutional earmarking that


                                                                                                    34

mandates governments at all three levels of their revenues in health and education. Inthe case of
Minas Gerais, current and investment expenditures were reduced in the first year, as described
elsewhere in this Program Document. However, much of the reduction fell on new investment
projects, rather maintenance of ongoing recurrent programs, and was accompanied by various
measures to improve efficiency and economy of these spendings (e.g., through improved
procurement). Besides, the government has explicitly protected the priority expenditure programs
including programs oriented toward poverty reduction such as Basic Sanitation, Family Health,
Basic Education, Minas Without Hunger, and Rural Electrification, to name a few.

Work at the national level suggests that the elasticity of poverty with respect to economic growth in
Brazil i s about one, and Minas is unlikely to be a significant exception to this statistical regularity
at the level of the country. Furthermore, there i s a 25% headcount ratio of poverty in the state.
This implies that a one percent increaseineconomic growth is likely to reducepoverty in Minas by
about a quarter of a percentagepoint per year, or one percent every four years.

Third, the improvements in the quality of public management in Minas will bring better service
delivery to the poor. Efforts such as results-based management and performance-based human
resource management are key in this regard. Effects have already been felt, such as the extension
of basic education in the state at no fiscal cost through more efficient mobilization of teachers and
school buildings.

Finally, both of the state's development agendas, the Plano Mineiro de Desenvolvimento Integrado,
or PMDI, as well as the Plano Plurianual de A@o Governamental, or PPAG, have incorporated
poverty reduction into their programs. Both these plans include the reduction of state-level social
inequalities as one of their primary objectives and programs. Inthe case of the PPAG, the program
lists objectives and sub-objectives related to poverty reduction and assigns each to various state-
level organizations which will be held responsible. It also lists the indicator that will be measured
(such as infrastructure and irrigation projects), the date by which the goal should be achieved, as
well as the financing requirements needed in order to obtain the objective. The PMDI also
highlightsthe reduction of inequalities as a requirement for more balanced growth within the state
of Minas Gerais. Illiteracy rates and infant mortality are some of the areas related to poverty
reduction that this plan proposes to tackle. Although the proposed operation, as a policy-based
DPL, would not be supporting these expenditure programs directly, the Bank's general budget
support would help the government fund and implement these programs adequately so as to achieve
desired policy outcomes, including poverty reduction.

Minas' development priorities, as embodied in the PMDI and the PPAG, reflect not only rigorous
technical analyses but also a genuinely participatory process of decision making. In both of the
state's development agendas, the state has encoded laws decreeing a participatory process,
including active participation of the civil society. The process for developing the PMDIis defined
in the state's constitution and was proposed by the Conselho de Desenvolvimento EconBmico e
Social (Council for Economic and Social Development).                This council is composed of
representatives from government, private sector, and civil society, with non-governmental
representatives comprising more than half of the council membership. Similarly with the PPAG,
the laws governing the plan require full transparency and public participation. The government's
PPAG proposal was discussed in public hearings at the legislative assembly's Commission on
Popular Participation, where some revisions based on citizen inputs were incorporated. The PPAG
i s reviewed annually by the same Popular ParticipationCommission, where the government reports
on the previous year's program performance.           Annual revisions to the plan also involve
dissemination via the internet.


                                                                                                    35

The state's participatory/consultative mechanisms are found at the program level as well. In their
rural development program, the state seeks to improve the quality of life of the target population
through small-scale social and economic infrastructure subproject investments, increasing the
social capital of the rural communities participating in the project by strengthening community
associations and municipal councils. By providing communities the opportunity to address their
needs through this process, the local-level municipal councils have succeeded in i)reducing
political interference at the local level; ii)strengthening the capacity of both communities and
municipal governments to select, prioritize, and implement investment decisions; iii)creating
partnerships between communities, municipal councils, and municipal governments and more
generally, increased the community voice in the use of public resources; and iv) fostering
citizenship through increased awareness of social responsibilities of citizens, their representatives
and public authorities incommunity and public matters.

The laws governing the publidprivate partnerships, supported by this operation, have stated that
public consultation i s requiredby law during the approval phase of a project. Furthermore, bidding
and contracting of a project must be open to the public. These laws provide further evidence of the
state's ability to ensure a broad, and therefore more effective, development approach.

Overall, there are grounds to conclude that (a) the proposed operation's poverty and social impacts,
which are expected to become significant over the medium term as implementation of the reforms
continues, will be positive; and (b) that the state government's policy framework, budget
arrangements, results-based management processes, and administrative capacity to manage its
policy measures' potential effects on poverty and social outcomes are deemed adequate.

B. ENVIRONMENTALASPECTS

The policies supported by this operation, includingnotably measures to strengthen the investment
climate and promote broad participation of private firms in infrastructure services provision, could
have significant positive environmental effects over the medium to long term. This operation
supports actions which will strengthen the government's capacity to monitor and manage those
effects.

The state of Minas Gerais is one of the three most advanced states in Brazil in terms of the
government capacity in environmental management, along with Paran6 and SBo Paulo, and boasts
of a well established Secretariat that leads Brazil in standards of environmental quality. The
federal government has put in place tripartite commissions which divide the responsibilities
between the municipalities, state, and the federal governments to ensure better enforcement of
environmentalregulations. Such a commission has beenput inplace inthe state of Minas Gerais.

Minas Gerais has qualified for the highest level of grant support under the Environmental Assets
component of the Bank-financedSecond National Environmental Project (NEP 11)by carrying out a
number of important reforms in a matrix of possible reforms. This matrix assigns points for a given
level of achievement in areas such as solid waste management, forest management, transparency,
etc. This level of qualification entitles the State to a grant of up to US$8 million which it will use
to support a project on the reduction of environmental impacts on the Rola Moca State Park. This
park encompasses much of the watershed that supplies water to the state capital of Belo Horizonte.
Activities include improvements in drainage, investments in fire prevention, development of
sewage and solid waste management and disposal, better protection of the park against violators, as
well as public education campaigns.


                                                                                                   36

Licensing has been among the core successful areas of environmental reform. Redesigning and
decentralizing environmental licensing is one of the reforms supported by this proposed operation.
The goal of the reform i s to strengthen the State Environment Secretariat (SEMAD) by replacing
the methods of environmental control that emphasized procedural compliance to one based on
active monitoring of environmental impacts and appropriate corrective measures in order to
promote sustainable development.

This objective has so far been realized through SIAM, Sistema Integrado de Informag6es
Ambientais (Integrated System for Environmental Information), a computerized tool to unify the
licensing of the "green," "brown," and "blue" agendas representing the areas of environmental
protection.   The reform has established an integrated system to aid in better environmental
management with a unified process for licensing, monitoring and control of the environment. The
system automatically determines the type and the extent of environmental assessment and
mitigation necessary for a particular project, once the works' profile i s entered into the system.
This user-friendly tool, financed through a grant which includes World Bank financing from the
NEP 11, allows detailed information on the local environment such as studies, analysis, and
licensing to be shared among all the users. Through this reform, the government i s reducing the
administrative cost to outside companies and i s establishing a simplified and more agile tool for
environmental management. Greater administrative efficiency in environmental licensing itself is
expected to free up the SEMAD's institutional resources for monitoring of environmental
conditions though indicators and on-site inspection.

One such improvement deals with compliance with environmental licensing. SEMAD has put in
place satellite photos and maps which aid officials in monitoring on-the-ground activities by
allowing instantaneous checking and matching of licenses via photos. Such improvements are
evidence of how SEMAD i s capitalizing on the administrative reforms (Choque de GestGo)
initiated by the state government and pushing to further upgrade their institutional capacities. A
number of decentralized agencies in the environment sector as well as one "structural project"
(Environmental Management in Minas 21StCentury) have signed results agreements and are
starting to adopt results-basedmanagement.37

The high level of environmental management capacity, including monitoring and accountability, is
applied to all projects undertaken in the State. It follows that with the development of the
publidprivate partnerships (PPP) component of this loan, the issue of environment will also be
addressed within the State's framework. To ensure this, the PPP partnership's managing council
includes the Secretary of Environment and Sustainable Development. Guidelines for PPP also
include public participation within the framework.

The environmental capacity of the state of Minas Gerais is of a reasonable and sound level to meet
the requirements of this operation.

C. PROGRAMIMPLEMENTATIONAND SUPERVISION

The Secretariat of Planning and Management (SEPLAG) will be responsible for overall
implementation of the proposed operation and for reporting progress and coordinating actions


37The environmentalagencies that have signedresultsagreements are IEF(Instituto Estadualde Florestas),
IGAM(Instituto Mineirode Gestiiode Aguas), andFEAM(Funda@oEstadualdo Meio Ambiente).



                                                                                                     37

between themselves and the Secretariats of Finance (SEF) and Economic Development (SEDE).
The Bank will monitor actions and review progress of implementation according to the matrix
conditions specified in Annex 2.

D. FIDUCIARY ASPECTS

The Country Financial Accountability Assessment (CFAA, 2002) concluded that at the national
level, Brazil's fiscal system provides reliable information and that adequate systems exist to
manage and track the receipt and use of public funds. It also noted that there existed a highlevel of
fiscal transparency. All these conditions support a development policy lending program. The
report concluded that the riskto both Bank and country funds was low.

To supplement the national CFAA, the Bank conducted in December 2004 a financial management
assessment (FMA) at the state level to further assess the health of Minas Gerais' financial
management arrangement. A detailed and comprehensive assessment, conducted in the FMA,
found that the government of Minas Gerais had established a comprehensive and functional set of
legal covenants, norms, and regulations for the management and control of public funds. It also
found that the government of Minas Gerais was committed to, adhering to and enforcing
compliance with, these requirements, including LRF covenants. To improve control activities, a
new internal audit system was institutionalized, which is currently in the initial implementation
phase. Furthermore, there is an adequate level of fiscal transparency and dissemination of public
information, in compliance with respective laws. Given this assessment, the Bank has concluded
that the systems are appropriate for the DPL. The FMA also made detailed recommendations for
possible improvements which have been shared with the government (see Box 3).

                                     ~~~               ~~~~

         Improvement inthe availability of civil servant personnel database
         Implementation of segregation of functions at the SIAFI's system level as a built-in feature and
         different levels of authority for the performance of transactions.
11.Accounting and FinancialReporting
         Improvement in the usability of the information produced by the S U F I system so as to allow better
         monitoring of progradproject performance.

         Technical recommendations include: a development freeze on all mainframe-based systems, redesign
         of the payroll system, and strengthening of web-based systems with more robust database platforms
         such as Oracle, improving widespread availability of managerial reports and production of non-
         technical manager readable documentation for every new major system feature, and use of proved IT
         architectural methodologies.

         methodology.

         procedures, release of public information, and clarification of the TCE-MG's role.




                                                                                                             38

These recommendations are being duly considered by the State of MG, which i s continuously
strengthening its PFM institutional capacity, including through the modernization of the State
Treasury Sub-secretariat which the proposed operation would support.

E. DISBURSEMENTAND AUDITING

The proposed loan will follow the Bank's disbursement proceduresfor development policy lending.
The untiedbalance of payment support will be disbursed against satisfactory implementationof the
development policy lending program and not tied to any specific purchases and no procurement
requirements will be needed. Once the loan is approved by the Board and becomes effective, the
proceeds of the first tranche will be deposited into a state of Minas Gerais Treasury Bank account
held with a commercial bank of the Borrower's choice. The Loan i s included in the 2006 State
Budget, and will be included in the 2007 Budget as well. The proceeds of the second tranche will
be deposited after all the conditions of the second tranche release are met. If, after depositing in
this account, the proceeds of the loan are used for ineligible purposes as defined by the
Development Loan agreement, IBRD will require the Borrower to either: a) return the amount of
the account for use for eligible purposes or b) refund the amount directly to IBRD.

The administrationof this loan will bethe responsibility of the Secretariat of Finance.

The IMF conducted a Safeguards Assessment of the Country in order to establish whether the
Central Bank's control, accounting, reporting and auditing systems are in place to manage
resources, including IMF disbursements, and that they are adequate to ensure integrity of
operations. The assessment was done in December 2003 and updated in March 2004. The
assessment concluded that the Central Bank does not present widespread vulnerabilities that could
compromise the safeguarding of Fund resources. In particular its audit i s conducted by an
internationally recognized audit firm, while its internal audit function contributes effectively to
internal control systems. Therefore from a fiduciary point of view, the control environment,
procedures and regulations governing the Bank's operations are generally adequate. Given that
there i s adequate knowledge about the soundness of the country's public financial management
system, additional fiduciary arrangements (such as using a dedicated Deposit Account) have not
been deemed necessary. The Central Bank duly acknowledged the receipt of the IMF report and
informed that some of IMF's recommendations were under implementation.

F. RISKSAND RISKMITIGATION

The main risks to the operation are assessedto be the following.

Implementationrisk: This risk that weak implementation of the agreed measures will result in a
significant delay of the second-tranche disbursement i s deemed to be low. The government has a
proven track record of achievements since taking office in January 2003, and most of the matrix
conditions were proposed by the government itself with a view to implementing them within the
mandate of the present government (till the end of 2006). Mitigationi s thus embedded in the loan
design, and will be furthered by close supervision and ongoing dialogue with the state authorities.

Politicalrisks. There is the risk that unforeseen political events cause a regime shift at the state
level leadingto backtrackingon core reforms supported by this loan. This risk i s deemed to be low
to moderate. The present government in Minas enjoys considerable popular support, in no small
part coming from its perceived seriousness about tackling some of the state's hardest problems


                                                                                                  39

head on. A logical way to mitigate this risk will be to make sure that the ongoing reforms produce
tangible results to the state's population with timely support with the proposed operation.

Fiscal risks. There is the risk that further economic changes at the national level - for example
related to general price inflation, which exerts powerful influences on the state government's
financial obligations to the National Treasury, or renewed economic instability - cause recent fiscal
gains in Minas to be undone or reversed. This risk i s deemed to be moderate for two reasons.
First, under the present federal government, Brazil's macroeconomic situation has strengthened
considerably, and in particular vulnerability to external shocks has declined significantly, as
described in the Recent Economic Developments section of this document.                 Second, more
specifically, the Central Bank's inflation targeting policy has now brought the country's main
inflation indicators back down below the levels at which they impose such unhealthy dynamics on
the state's finances. Risk mitigation in this context consists of the Bank's very strong relationship
with both the Ministry of Finance and the Central Bank of Brazil, and ongoing programmatic DPL
supporting both fiscal reforms and microeconomic growth-promoting reforms at the national level.
Further mitigation of fiscal risks is taking place at the state level through formal and informal
technical advice relating to the state's social security system, minimizing future judicial debts
(precatdrios), and strengthening the financial position of the state civil-service health plan, the last
of these being supported duringproject preparation.

Finally, a risk to the success of the state's PPP framework i s that the national framework for PPP
proves an inadequate supporting structure. The state's PPP law and regulation duly leave certain
roles for federal law and regulation to cover. Since PPP remains a new initiative in Brazil with no
track record to speak of to date, this risk i s deemed to be moderate to high. Mitigation comes in
two forms. First, the Bank i s actively supporting the design and implementationof the federal PPP
initiative through the programmatic loans for sustainable and equitable growth and associated TA.
Second, the design of the PPP framework in Minas Gerais is such as to minimize the fiscal risks
implied by state partnerships with the private sector. In this connection, close coordination with
the technical staff of the IDB,who are directly involved inPPPproject design inMinas Gerais, will
be an additional risk mitigation strategy.

Parceriasptiblico-privadas

As parcerias publico-privadas (PPPs) representamuma inovaqzo na forma de o Estado
promover a oferta de infra-estrutura e disponibilizar serviqos publicos, atravds da
iniciativa privada. Esse modelo busca aperfeiqoar os instrumentos de contrataqiio

moderna para enfrentar o grande desafio de suplantar o deficit de investimento publico
em areas essenciais, como transportes, saneamento e saude. Como projeto autanomo,
consiste em importante ferramenta para o enfrentamento da demanda por investimentos
numcontexto de crise fiscal.

Considerando-se o contexto de restriggo fiscal e buscando retomar investimentos em
areas essenciais para o desenvolvimento econbmico e social do Estado atraves da

                  ANNEX 1:LETTER OF DEVELOPMENTPOLICY

                             LETTER DEVELOPMENT
                                     OF                POLICY



OF.GAB.SEC/l16/2006
                                                           Belo Horizonte, March 6, 2006.

Mr.PaulWolfowitz
President
The World Bank
Washington, DC


Dear Mr.Wolfowitz,

This Letter of DevelopmentPolicy presents the measuresby the State Government of Minas
Gerais for fiscal adjustment, public sector improvement, and promotion of private sector
development. We request World Bank support for these measures and financial assistance
in the form of a development policy loan. The loan proceeds, which are expected to be
released in two tranches, will support reforms and measures in priority areas, strengthening
the execution of the GERAES Program as well as the management o f State debt, in
observance of State Law no15.521 dated June 6, 2005, regulated by Decree no44.181 of
December 22,2005.

Backgroundof the Stateof MinasGerais

Until 2003, Minas Gerais was faced with one of the worst fiscal situations in the country.
The state budget that year registered a deficit of approximately R$2.3 billion, which was
balanced with improbable capital revenue estimates. Budget and financial execution were
inconsistent with each other - which led to debts and linear and indiscriminate budget cuts
of operation and maintenance as well as investment budgets. The government strategies, in
this context, could not be carried out, which resulted in inefficient public services and
unfavorable investment climate. The strategy of the Government of Minas Gerais, defined
in 2003, therefore, is based on two premises:     fiscal responsibility and the need for a
development agenda that justified to the society the initial adjustments of expenditure
reduction (rationalization) and revenue increase.

The short-term administrative reforms implemented at the beginning of 2003 enabled the
Government to construct a development agenda for the State, with active participation of
government authorities and representatives o f organized civil society: private sector,
workers and non-governmental organizations.      Named Mineiro Integrated Development
Plan (Plano Mineiro de Desenvolvimento Integrado - PMDI) and turned into a law in
January 2004, this agenda was built on the basis of a broad diagnosis of the State. The
diagnosis encompassed the State's economic and social dimensions, the situation of the




                                                                                          41

public sector, and identified key bottlenecks and decisive opportunities to initiate the cycle
of development.

The diagnosis demonstrated the viability of the vision of "Minas as the best state to live and
invest in" by 2020. Inthis sense, three strategic guidelines are fundamental: (i)  reorganize
the state public sector with a new management model; (ii)    carry out fiscal adjustment; and
(iii)promote economic development in innovative ways. These guidelines, therefore,
constitute the three pillars of the Programfor which we wish to seek World Bank support.

The New Management Model


The adoption of a new management model, geared toward optimizing results for the
society, molded the administrative reform and modernization of planning and management
tools of the State. This new model foresees strengthening of planning and design of
incentive mechanisms to align the State's organizations around the proposed strategy. The
implementation of this management model required changes inthe administrative structure,
modernization of planning mechanisms, and introduction of good practices in the
management of human resources, physical assets, equipment, and information technology.


Aspects of the Administrative Reform


The Administrative Reform implemented inMinas Gerais was aimed at adjusting the public
administration to the new management model. It was institutionalized with the passageof a
set of 63 laws delegated in January, 2003. It was from this legal frame mark that the
Governmental Management Collegiate Body (Colegiado de Gestco Governamental) was
established as a first step toward the reform of the State. The Collegiate body, presided by
the Governor, with the participation of the State Secretaries, aims to ensure coherence
among the government's strategic formulation and the execution of public policies. The
body i s composed of three thematic cabinets - the Cabinet for Coordination, Planning,
Management and Finance Chamber (Cdmara de Coordena@o Gera, Planejamento, Gestio
e FinanCas - CCGPGF), the Cabinet for Economic Development and Infrastructure
(Cdmara de Desenvolvimento EconSmico e Infra-estrutura - CDEI) and the Cabinet for
Social Development and Citizenship (Cdmara de Desenvolvimento Social e Cidadania -
CDSC).


The State secretariats were redesigned according to a result-based management model. Six
secretariats were closed, in addition to 43 super-intendancies in the Direct Administration,
16 departments in the Indirect Administration, and 388 administrative units in the Direct
and Indirect Administration and, consequently, 1,326 commissioned offices were
eliminated. The duties of General Planning and Coordination were merged with those of
Human Resources and Administration, thus creating the State Secretariat of Planning and
Management (Secretaria de Estado de Planejamento e Gestgo - SEPLAG), which unifies
planning, management and budget.


                                                                                            42

This same management model was adopted with the creation of the Minas Gerais
Development Company (Companhia de Desenvolvimentode Minus Gerais - CODEMIG) -
which incorporatedduties regarding support to development that were previously dispersed,
as well as upon the creation of the Advocacia Geral do Estado - AGE, (State Attorney's
Office), the State's Ombudsman Services (Ouvidoria-Geral do Estado - OGE) and the
State's General Auditing Service (Auditoria Geral do Estado - AUGE) (with the creation of
an auditing unit in all organizations and entities of the Public Administration).


Simultaneous to the restructuring of organizations, other measures necessary for the
creation of a new public management environment followed, such as:


    Centralization of payroll at SEPLAG (Decree No. 43188 of February 10, 2003) to
    facilitate control and correction of distortions inthe benefits granted to employees;

    Implementation of the System for the Administration of Personnel in the State of Minas
    Gerais (Sistemade Adrninistra@o de Pessoal do Estado de Minus Gerais - SISAP) that
    allowed for management of personnel payments;
    Creation, following the logic of the proposed management model, of the new career
    structure that regrouped the State's civil servants into 14 groups.
   Implementation of Decree no43.699 of December 11, 2003 related to the Integrated
    System for the Administration of Goods and Services of the State of Minas Gerais
    (SistemaIntegrado de Administrqlio de Materiais e SewiGos de Minas Gerais - SIAD),
   which i s integrated with the System for Financial Administration (Sistema de
   Administrqlio Financeira - SZAFZ) allowing better management of contracting
   expenses with the due budgetary/financial estimates and the regulation of the system of
   price registry, general roster of suppliers and of procurement processes for the
   acquisition of goods and services that are common;
   Development of the Electronic Governance program the objective of which i s to
   modernize public sector management and democratize information so as to allow more
   and better service to the people;
   Creation of the Strategic Management of State Resources and Actions (Gestlio Estratkgica
   de Recursos e Apjes do Estado - GERAES), which identifies and prioritizes the
   Government's main strategy in terms of resource allocation and management, as
   reflected in the "Structural Projects;" confirming to Decree no43.554 of August 28,
   2003.
   Adoption of the Results Agreements and the Organizational Performance Evaluation as
   mechanisms to implement the results-based management model;
   Creation of a new legal structure for provision of services that are relevant for the public
   in partnership with the private sector and the organized civil society, notably the
   implantation and dissemination of OSCIP (Organizqio da Sociedade Civil de
   Interesse Pu'blico - OSCIP) model and o f the PPP.




                                                                                           43

These measures sum up the need and strong will of the State to promote a redesign of the
institutional architecture of Public Administration as a basis for the re-creation of a State
that i s permeable to heterogeneous interests and that i s prepared to live harmoniously with
diversity and to administer it democratically and in an agile manner that yields lower costs
to society. The Bank's technical and financial support to these initiatives will be very
important for the institutionalization of a new management model.


Strategic Management of State Resourcesand Actions (Gestiio Estrate`gica de Recursos
e A@es do Estado - GERAES)


The main challenges taken on by the Minas Gerais Integrated Development Plan (PMDI)
are to foster fiscal adjustment, ensure efficient delivery of public services, and focus
investments toward strategic areas. In terms of fiscal adjustment, annual deficit figures
show the government's unconditional commitment to fiscal austerity. However, SEPLAG
acknowledges that linear and indiscriminate adjustment of government expenses - a normal
practice in the public sector - does not lead to a structural and permanent adjustment and
that, in general, it indiscriminately sacrifices governmental actions.


Inthis sense, while trying to define actions that would lead to long-termfiscal equilibrium,
with revenue increase, expenditure reduction, and debt management, the Government
created an institutional framework in 2003 to ensure the execution of structural projects
without hindering fiscal balance.       The following laws and regulations comprise this
institutional framework: the PMDI, the Pluriannual Plan (Plano Plurianual de Gestiio -
PPAG), the Law of Budgetary Guidelines (Lei de Diretrizes Orpmentdrias - LDO), the
Annual Budget Law (Lei Orpzmentdria Anual - LOA) and the Decree for Budgetary and
Financial Programming (Decreto de ProgramaGiio Orpmentdria e Financeira).
Complementary, and particular to Minas Gerais, the Board for Budgetary and Financial
Programming (Junta de Programa@io Orpmentdria e Financeira - JPOF) i s a committee
composed of members of the Secretariats of Finance and o f Planning and Management,
which provides a permanent deliberative body over the afore-mentioned legal tools,
monitoring results and which may, at any time, mandate corrective measures.


The operationalization of this framework begins with the definition of fiscal targets. In
other words, the process first defines the volume of resources that the state has available for
its expenses. The Strategic Management of State Resources and Actions (GERAES) were
designed to avoid undue resource dispersion, and resulting inefficiencies in government
actions. GERAES comprises the 34 structural projects chosen in the PMDI and enacted in
the PPAG and LOA, intended to work as catalysts for the development of the state. These
projects include, among other areas, the Modernization of the State Secretariat of Finance,
the "Choque de Gestiio" (administrative reform), government planning and budgeting,
electronic governance, infrastructure, public-private partnerships and management of public
security services. The structural projects are subject to intensive management and have a
guaranteed flow of resources, an important element inthe environment of fiscal adjustment.



                                                                                            44

In implementing the "Structural Projects," project management techniques, which are
common in the private sector, are used. Efforts are made to align all those involved toward
the proposed final results.     For project management, the Unit for Support of Project
Management (Unidade de Apoio e Gestio de Projetos - UAGP) was created in the
Secretariat of Planning and Management, with usual roles of planning, monitoring, support
and evaluation of the structural projects, but in innovative ways. The UAGP also defines
budgetary and financial flows in all stages - budgeting, monthly releases of resources, and
reallocation o f resources between projects based on performance.


Inthe short run, the expected effect of GERAES, through the results of each one of the
structural projects, i s to reinforce the fiscal adjustment while maintaining strategic
investments. There i s consistency in this expectation because: i)the pre-condition for the
resource allocation i s fiscal balance; ii)the strategic focus established in the GERAES
increases effectiveness of the projects; and iii)some of the projects have immediate impact
on revenue increases and current expenditure reductions.


To improve this model of planning, the key action i s institutionalization of the new
planning and budgeting process and harmonization of these functions, primarily by adding
the management model for the Structural Projects to the State's corporate information
systems.


Management Modernization


The Structural project "Choque de Gestio: People, Quality and Innovation in the Public
Administration" revitalizes the state's management model by guiding it towards the
attainment of results based on quality, productivity and on criteria that create incentives for
greater commitment on behalf of those involved. It foresees investments in the training of
state employees and the adoption of new models of public-private partnerships for the better
rendering of services to citizens.


It i s structured upon the following pillars:

      Strategic alignment that enables visualization of the degree of complexity of the
     organization's agenda, the convergence o f government strategies, and institutional
     strengthening. Furthermore, it focuses on the convergence between the government
     strategies and the organizations' strategies and their need for institutional strengthening.
     This alignment process i s vital for integrating the processesof planning and government
     management. It reflects the perspectives o f the interested parties and emphasizes the
     involvement of personnel following the legal framework and the sectoral public
     policies.
     Individual performance evaluation of the employee conditioned to tenure, as well as
     performance measurement and rewards by means of objectively measured criteria. This


                                                                                              45

    evaluation process was started in July of 2004, and through it more than 5,000
    employees have received face-to-face training in how to apply this evaluation method,
    and close to 18,000 employees have learned the method through distance-learning.
    Additional compensation based on performance (Adicional de Desempenho -ADE) as a
    substitute for time-in-service compensation for all employees that were contracted by
    the state after July of 2003, which has added 11,321 employees as of August 2005 under
    this new model. For the employees that were hired up to the fore-mentioned date, the
    ADE is optional.
    Organizational performance evaluation, following the definition of targets to be met by
    the government entities through results agreements. The agreements give the entities
    management flexibility and increase their financial and budgetary autonomy. As of this
    moment, 17 results agreements have been signed, and of these, at least five are being
    improved in a revision process.
    Implementation of the shared ("joined-up,')      public administration model with the
    organized civil society. The adoption, in the State, of the OCSIP model i s intended to
    turn civil society into a co-participantinpolicy implementation, especially inareas such
    as health, education, social assistance, environmental protection, development of new
    technologies, promotion of amateur sports, culture, among others.            So far, six
    partnership agreementshave already been signed.
Inthe areaof humanresources, besides these actions, all of the state'scareer structures were
reformulated.    In 2003, 16 Bills of Law (Projetos de Lei) were sent to the legislative
assembly (ALEMG)for the reformulation of state careers so as to transform the 893 classes
into 131 careers, by eliminating 80,187 and creating 43,617 positions. All of these Bills
have been approved and sanctioned.

The Government i s developing information technology as a complement to the
"Management Shock." Thus, development of a new payment system i s under way. This
new system will be fully integrated with the State Personnel Administration System
(Sistema de Administra@o de Pessoal - SISAP), currently in a phase of data entry into the
database. This new payment system, fully calibrated and using relational databases, will
eliminate duplicate data entries and storage that still exist today, and will be user friendly
due to automatic calculation of pays and benefits, as well as through user support, which is.
currently not available.

Furthermore, an informational system for monitoring individual performance evaluation i s
being designed, which will enable secure and efficient management of the evaluation
process in the State. This process will be continuous, suffer less from inconsistencies, and
offer easy access to information.

Inorder to rationalize supply management, the Government of the State of Minas Gerais
implemented the Integrated System for Administration of Goods and Services (Sistema
Integrado de Administra@o de Materiais e ServiEos- SIAD) on January 1,2004. SLAD is
a corporate system which, through integration with the Financial Management System
(Sistemade AdministrapTo Financeira - SIAFI) and other State systems, enables control of


                                                                                           46

the cycle of goods and services management, from procurement to the point where the
goods are distributed, accounted for as government assets, and the services are completed.
This tool has been a great facilitator of the achievement of the fiscal adjustment targets
related to supply management.

The Government intends to install new modules for procurement and management of
contracted goods and services, especially one that would allow for the price registry to be
usedingovernment purchases and contracting with the reverse auction @regLio)modality.


Modernization of the State Finance Administration


Both expansion of tax revenues of Minas Gerais and improvement infinancial management
form the core of fiscal adjustment, and are translated into the Structural Project of State
Finance Administration. The project consists of investments in physical infrastructure and
logistics, modernization of administrative, tax and financial processes, as well as
improvement intaxpayer services to create a better investment climate inthe State.


Better taxpayer services, especially through electronic government, are guided by the goal
of fully implementing a new information system in 2007.


Planning and execution of revenue collection efforts today follows a matrix approach,
which i s detailed in the Master Plan for Fiscal Action (Plano Diretor da A@o Fiscal).
These actions are also reflected in the Results Agreement signed on August 11, 2004 by
SEFand SEPLAG, andrevisedin2005 and 2006.


The targets are being met, as demonstrated inthe increase in the State's relative share of the
ICMS tax collected, which today corresponds to 85% of the tax revenues in Minas Gerais,
of the national total. The COTEPE/CONFAZ data show that the relative share of the State
inthe collection of this tax has changed from 9.1% of the national total in 2002 to 10.1% in
2005. This i s because the tax collection in Minas has been rising at a pace faster than in the
rest of the country and above the performance of the economic activities inthe State.


The continuous increase inthe state revenues, along with the gains from better management
of public spending, has led to a qualitative change in Minas Gerais' fiscal indicators.
According to the assessment under the Fiscal Restructuring and Adjustment Program which
the State maintains with the National Treasury Secretariat (STN) following the Federal Law
9,496 of 1997, the tendency i s for the State to generate increasing primary surplus and
reduce the ratio of personnel expenditures to the net current revenues (RCL).38 The primary
surplus increased from R$665 million in 2002 to R$ 1,157 million in 2003, reaching R$
1,263 million in 2004. The ratio of personnel expenditures to RCL was reduced from


38According to Offcio No8143/2005 COREM/STNof December 16,2005.


                                                                                            47

71.33% in 2002 to 67.17% in the following year, to 61.01% in 2004. For 2005, the agreed
goals are R$ 1,596 million in of primary surplus and 61,20% of the personnel expenditure
indicator, which will be assessed inthe next STNmission to Minas Gerais planned in 2006.


The improvement in the fiscal situation of Minas Gerais also allowed the Government to
regularize its debts owed to suppliers,through various measures, including the payments of
R$ 441 million in 2003 and R$ 611 million in 2004, for outstanding floating debts from
previous fiscal years.39


Financial support from the World Bank will make resources available not only for
continuation o f the structural project for the State Finance Administration, but also for
improving the profile of the State's consolidated and floating debts through pre-payments of
R$100 million inthese categories.


Public-PrivatePartnerships


Public-private partnerships (PPPs) represent an innovation in the provision of public
services by means of private initiative. This model strives to improve the contracting tools
used by the Public Administration and to make these tools compatible with the interests of
society as well as provide economic returns for the private sector. PPPs are a modern
means to address the deficit in public investments in essential areas such as transportation,
basic sanitation, and health. Autonomously, PPP constitutes an important tool for dealing
with demand for investments inthe context of fiscal crisis.


Considering the context of fiscal restrictions and trying to recapture investments in areas
essential for the State's economic and social development through service contracts, Minas
Gerais created the State Program of Public-Private Partnerships, via the Law No. 14,868 of
December 16, 2003. Minas Gerais was the first state in Brazil to adopt a specific legal
framework for PPPs, in order to consolidate and institutionalizethis mechanism.


The PPP Unit (set forth by Decree No. 43702 of December 26, 2003) i s responsible for
coordinating the program and for organizing and disseminating concepts and methodologies
that are unique to PPP. Another responsibility o f the Unit i s to advise the Management
Council of Public-Private Partnerships (Conselho Gestor de Parcerias Pziblico Privadas -
CGPPP), which i s headed by the state governor. The CGPPP i s responsible for selecting
and approving PPP projects in Minas Gerais, as well as for the elaboration of the State Plan
for Public-Private Partnerships.




39Accordingto Oficio no228106-A of February20,2006 of STEISEFaddressed to the World BankMundial


                                                                                             48

After the approval of the PPP Law inMinas Gerais in 2003, five pilot projects were defined
in different areas to start the program. The selected areas are: infrastructure and public
transportation (recovery and enlargement of the infrastructure of highway MG-050 that
connects the east of S5o Paulo state to the capital of Minas Gerais); public security and the
penitentiary system (provision of 3000 new prison places - including services for the
construction and operation of the units); basic sanitation (provision of basic sanitation
services in municipalities that have low levels of human development); science and
education (construction and operation of the State University of Minas Gerais campus in
Belo Horizonte); and urban management and development (construction and operation of
the State Government's Administrative Center inBelo Horizonte).


Detailed designs of these projects which define their economic and financial structure, are
imperative and have been carried out by consulting firms with broad international
experience in PPPs. The first of these, for the highway infrastructure project (MG-050) was
contracted in December 2004, with KPMG Consultores Associados as the project leader.
The second design work, for the prison construction project, has also been contracted, and
i s being carried out by PricewaterhouseCoopers.


The other fundamental point for operationalization of the PPPs refers to the guarantee
component. In this area, besides the consultancies for project designs, the State contracted
consulting services of UNIBANCO (Uniiio de Buncos Brusileiros S.A).,which, along with
Levy & Salomiio Advogados e Caixa de Dep6sitos de Portugal, are designing the guarantee
arrangement for the Estate Program of Public-Private Partnerships.        This study, which
defines the guarantee mechanism to be adopted and the legal instruments for its creation,
will be finalized before the second-tranche releases of this loan. Inaddition, the publication
of the official announcement of the first PPP project of the State, as well as the conclusion
of the Operations Manual of the Structural Program of Public-Private Partnerships, which
will establish procedures for the processing and the choice of PPP projects by the CGPPP,
should take place in 2006.


The financial support by the World Bank will contribute to strengthening of the State
Program of Public-Private Partnerships, specifically to the effort to capitalize the guarantee
fund. The Government estimates that R$ 100 million of the resources made available by
the Bank will be allocated for this effort of capitalization.


Optimization of thepublic services in security


In pursuit of providing social safety as a public good indelible from the set of State
obligations, Minas Gerais emerges in the national scene with the project to integrate police
actions, with emphasis on installation of the Integrated System for Social Defense (SIDS).
The program involves civil and military police and the Military Firefighting Corps working
at the Center for Integrated Assistance to Citizens (Centro Integrado de Atendimento do


                                                                                           49

Cidadiio e Despacho - CIAD). Similarly, the areas of policing have been integrated to
encourage overlap of policing districts by the Civil and the Military Police.


This integration of public security services allows better allocation of resources and
reliability of the crime data, and thus reduction in response time and increased capacity to
respond to the citizens. Additionally, essential actions include professionalization of, and
the increase in the number of places in, the prison system; professionalization of services to
juvenile delinquents; social prevention of criminality, with the flagship Program Fiva Vico
("Stay Alive"), which i s currently supported by the World Bank - the pilot program
introduced in the Aglomerado Morro das Pedras region, reduced the homicide rate by 47%
in six months; and implantation of the nucleus for homicide control in the areas of high
incidence.


The Integrated System of Social Defense (Sistema Zntegrado de Defesa Social - SIDS) can
be defined as a system for managing information on social defense, which enables
integration and sharing of information by the entities responsible for public security. Its
objective i s to provide integrated responses and dispatch in police cases (PM / PC) and by
firefighters, as well as the follow-up to these events, reporting, complaint of crimes, or
representation up to accusation and execution of penalty. The system will cover the entire
State and i s being implemented in stages.          The first stage of the program i s the
implementationof CIAD, which i s already installed inthe Base of the General Command of
the Military Police of Minas Gerais (Quartel do Comando Geral da Policia Militar de
Minas Gerais - CPMMG).           The other stages are in progress, and are sub-divided into
phases, with various intermediate events for secure implementation. These events include
the implantation of the Registry of Social Defense Events (Registro de Eventos de Defesa
Social - REDS), Data Storage, Spacial Statistics, the Module of Response and Dispatch,
and the Remote Electronic Registry of Police Cases.


The program Integrated Areas (Areas Zntegradas) consists of implementation of a results-
based policing methodology inBelo Horizonte and the Belo Horizonte Metropolitan Region
through definition of a shared territorial responsibility.     In this way, this program is
harmonized with the implantation of SIDS in integrating police actions by offering to the
society: (i) reduction in response time in police and fire emergencies; (ii) expansion of the
capacity to respond; (iii) possibility for the citizen to follow up on the State's action with
respect to police and fire emergencies; (iv) expanded collection of information, which will
provide better support to investigations; and, (v) improvement in the mechanisms for
follow-up and control of the actions of the entities involved in social defense. After the
definition of the district of the integrated areas of Belo Horizonte and the Belo Horizonte
Metropolitan Region, began its physical implementation and in December 2005 the first
integrated area of the Capital startingfunctioning.


Altogether, the programs and their diverse actions have progressively achieved the expected
results in relation to violent crimes. From August, 2004, the reported incidence of violent


                                                                                           50

crimes remained stable, after eight years of growth, and up until November 2005, there was
a reduction of 17% in violet crimes in the State capital compared to the same period in
2004.


The support o f the World Bank can support the actions of the program, especially in the
implementation of the integrated areas of policing the Belo Horizonte Metropolitan Region,
and in the interior, in the development of the remaining modules of SIDS, and in the
dissemination of measures of social prevention of crime.


Estrada Real


The Project Estrada Real i s one of the principal actions of the Government for job creation
and income generation in the service sector, covering some of the most weakened regions
of the State. Institutionally, the consolidation of the Estrada Real Project requires support
to and training of local agents in the tourism sector, and greater promotion and publicity of
their tourism attractions.


On the other hand, the provision of infrastructure services along the Estrada Real i s
identified as the key condition for development of sustainable tourism. It i s necessary to
recuperate and maintain 800 Kmof access routes in the area of influence of Estrada Real, at
an estimated cost of R$ 40 million, and for COPASA to expand sanitation services -
220,000 residences for water supply and 252,000 residences that lack sewage.             The
participation of the World Bank will certainly be fundamental.


Innovative Promotionfor SustainableDevelopment


The Competitive Business of Minas (Empresa Mineira Competitiva) structural project's,
cornerstone i s the Fucilita Minas program (set forth by Decree No. 43656 of November 21,
2003), the implementation of which i s in its advanced stages. Its objective i s to provide,
through the offer of better channels of access to the state, solutions to facilitate the
operation, expansion and modernization of established business, as well as start of new
businesses in Minas Gerais, including areas such as tax, credit, environmental regulations,
infrastructure, and the registration of businesses.


The segments of priority access for firms refer to tax matters, credit, environmental
regulation, infrastructure, and company registration.


Starting in January of 2004, as set forth by Law No. 15.219 of July 7, 2004, Simples Minas
provides differentiated treatment in the administrative,         tax, credit, and business
development fields to micro businesses, small businesses and to autonomous entrepreneurs.


                                                                                          51

The system that was adopted eliminated the need for the use of tax records as it considers
only purchases by taxpayers for the purpose of calculating ICMS. It also eliminated the
need to call on the taxpayer to verify compliance with fiscal obligations. It makes use of the
progressive table to calculate the ICMS. It also offers tax citizenry to those that are on the
outskirts of fiscal legality or who work informally as it institutes the concept of the
autonomous entrepreneur. The estimate i s that it reaches out to 255 thousand active
taxpayers.


Virtual access of medium and large-scale taxpayers to the State Revenue Agency i s being
implemented by means of the Integrated Administration System of the Revenue Agency
(Sistema Integrado de Adrninistraqio du Receita - SIARE). Since January 2005, on-line
services are being offered for taxpayer registration, change in and removal from the
taxpayer registry; transmission of magnetic files; in addition to services regarding requests
for tax documentation and transfer.       Furthermore, the system i s integrated with the
databases of other entities that hold fiscal information (Receita Federal, ANP, CRC,
ABIGRAF, etc.).      The SIARE also covers ITCD declarations.          In 2006, requests for
authorization for issuance of tax documents and certidiio de de'bitos tributiirios (certificate
of tax debits?) will be included, thus comprising seven new modules in total to be made
available to all.   The ICMS taxpayer registry i s being integrated with the registry of
suppliers to the State - SIAD, so as to prevent taxpayers from having to provide the same
information to the State in different systems and Secretariats. It i s also foreseen that the
State Revenue Sub-secretariat will have direct access to the registries of Junta Comercial
(JUCEMG) and their databases will be integrated with each other. The goal i s to ease
administrative-tax procedures, with gradual offer of new services on the internet, which
should encourage cost reduction for the taxpayers and for the State Revenue Sub-
secretariat, as well as with the improvement in taxpayer services. Additionally, adoption of
virtually secure mechanisms in the State-taxpayer relations will improve tax administration
and audits.


InOctober, 2005, the Minas Fcicil was started. This program brings together different
entities of the State and the Municipal Governments in the same physical space, and thus
enables taxpayers to obtain their records from all the entities in one step, in observance of
Decree no44.106 of September 14,2005.


Another highlight in the tax segment i s the Investe Minas project whose objective i s to
make use of accumulated ICMS credit, including mechanisms of transfers between
businesses to strengthen private investments.


As a result, the Facilitu Minus has simplified the concession of loans to micro and small
businesses from funds managed by the BDGM and reduced the number of documents
required of the interested party from 25 to 3. Inaddition, the loan processing i s now done by
means of the internet. As regards environmental regulation, the SEMAD Call Center
(Central de Atendimento SEMADBDMG) was created in 2003. Since then, the


                                                                                            52

businessmenthat ask the BDMGfor financing also receive orientation so that their projects
are in accordance to the norms for environmental licensing.


Furthermore, it i s important to highlight that the challenge of sustainable development in
Minas Gerais i s concentrated on the improvement of an environmental regulations. The
Environmental Management of the 21st Century (Gesta"o Arnbientul do Se'culo XXI)
structural project, aims to decentralize environmental management and to carry out strategic
environmental assessments, especially in the areas of infrastructure and economic
development. The decentralization of management began with the issuance of Decree no
43.278 of April 22, 2003 in 2003 and, up to now, seven out of the eight Regional Councils
for Environmental Policies (ConselhosRegionuis de Poli'tica Arnbientul) have been legally
instituted. The Integrated System for the Environment (Sisternu Integrudo de Meio
Ambiente - SIAM) i s in its final stages of implementation. It allows free access to the large
database of regional environmental data and already functions as the only manager of the
state's environmental licensing.


All of SIAM will be integrated to the environmental indicators that will also be
implemented duringthe first semester of 2006. Once they are selected, a periodic measuring
of these indicators will be carried out and such data will be added to SIAM's database so as
for all activities of the state's environmental organizations to refer to these indicators.


Requestfor FinancialAssistance


The Government of Minas Gerais remains firmly committed to its program of reforms,
fiscal adjustment and structural projects outlined above and would welcome World Bank
financial assistance. We appreciate the prompt consideration of a development policy loan,
in two stages, in support of the measures that have already been adopted and those which
are under implementation.


Sincerely yours,




AntGnio August0 Junho Anastasia
State Secretary
