                            ANNEX 3: FUNDRELATIONSNOTE

Public Information Notice (PIN) No. 05/166, December 16,2005
IMFExecutiveBoardConcludes 2005 Post-ProgramMonitoring Discussionswith Brazil

On December 7, 2005, the Executive Board of the International Monetary Fund (IMF) concluded
Post-Program Monitoring discussions with Brazil based on the information available through that
date.

Background- Notwithstanding the difficult political context since May 2005, macroeconomic
performance has remained robust, underpinned by strong macroeconomic policies and favorable
external conditions. After slowing in the fourth quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005,
economic activity rebounded strongly in the second quarter, before declining markedly in the third
quarter of 2005, mainly reflecting inventory decumulation. As a result, real GDP grew by an
average of 2% percent (year-on-year) during the first three quarters of 2005. Growth has remained
supported by private consumption-reflecting       steady gains in real incomes and employment, and
rapid growth in household credit-and by net exports.

The strong fiscal performance of recent years has continued, with the consolidated primary fiscal
surplus above the 2005 target. This improvement reflects continued strong tax collections-
particularly income taxes-as      well as higher primary surpluses of subnational governments and
public sector enterprises. However, pension imbalances have continued to grow. The prudent
tightening of monetary policy initiatedin September 2004 and the appreciation of the exchange rate
helped bringthe 12-month headline inflation down from a peak of 8 percent in May to 6.4 percent
in October. With inflation pressures abating and inflation expectations virtually converging to the
end-2005-06 targets, the central bank has lowered its policy interest rate since September, by a
total of 125 basis points to l8?hpercent.

The balance of payments position has remained strong. Export performance has continued to
exceed expectations, supported by rapid global growth and highcommodity prices, notwithstanding
the appreciation of the real in real effective terms since early 2005. Private capital inflows have
also strengthened, driven by higher foreign direct investment and renewed portfolio net inflows.
Brazilian corporates have continued to deleverage and external debt has declinedfurther.

Public sector net debt has declined further and its structure has improved further. Several important
steps were taken to improve the maturity profile and extend the duration of public debt, including
the issuance for the first time of a US$1.5 billion 10-year real-denominated external sovereign
bond in September. Nevertheless, the share of floating-rate domestic debt remains high and, while
improving at the margin, the averageduration of public debt is still short. The central bank resumed
intervention in the foreign exchange market in early October aimed at further building up
internationalreserves, which have continued to rise relative to short-term external debt.

Against this backdrop, financial market sentiment has remained favorable, albeit with bouts of
volatility. The real attained its highest level since early 2001, sovereign bond spreads narrowed to
all time lows, and stock prices reached historical highs. Since mid-October, Moody's upgraded
Brazil's sovereign credit rating in line with other credit rating agencies, while other credit rating
agencies have upgraded the outlook from stable to positive.

The strong macroeconomic performance, together with the increased coverage of the Bolsa Familia
program, has led to a significant reduction in poverty and income inequality between 2002-04. The


                                                                                                  57

poverty rate has declined to its lowest level since 1992, with the share of people below the poverty
line decliningto 25.1 percent in 2004, from 27.3 percent in 2003, well below the 35.9 percent rate
in 1992. The strengthening of the Bolsa Familia program, along with higher employment in the
formal labor market, allowed for a significant improvement inthe income of the poorest groups and
for a reduction in the income gap between formal and informal workers for the first time in the
decade. Income inequality has also declined to its lowest level since 1981.

ExecutiveBoardAssessment

Executive Directors commended the Brazilian authorities for the impressive performance of the
economy since the end of the stand-by arrangement. Directors attributed this performance to the
authorities' commitment to sustain and strengthen the macroeconomic policy framework and to the
comprehensive reforms implemented over the past several years, together with supportive external
conditions. The combination of high public sector primary surpluses, inflation targeting, and a
flexible exchange rate regime has proven highly successful in reducing vulnerabilities and keeping
financial market confidence high, despite uncertain political conditions. Directors also commended
the authorities for the significant progress made in reducing poverty in recent years, thus enabling
Brazil to continue lowering income inequality and to make progress toward achieving the
MillenniumDevelopment Goals.

Directors viewed the Brazilian economy as well placed for continued favorable economic
performance. Following buoyant economic growth in 2004, the economy has expanded at a more
sustainable pace in 2005. Export performance has remained strong, notwithstanding the marked
appreciation of the real, while on the domestic side rising employment and real incomes have
boosted consumer expenditures. Directors noted the unfavorable outcome for GDP in the third
quarter, but observed that this seemed to reflect mainly inventory adjustment and other specific
factors, and that the underlyingtrend of domestic demand remains positive.

With balance sheet vulnerabilities still a concern and the risks posed by the external and domestic
environment, Directors welcomed the authorities' commitment to sustain strong policies. Public
debt remains high and of relatively short maturity, with a large share still linked to short-term
interest rates. Along with sizable external borrowing needs, these factors still leave the Brazilian
economy exposedto abrupt changes in global conditions and the domestic political scene.

Directors commended the prudent conduct of monetary policy in the context of inflation targeting
and a flexible exchange rate policy. Inflation i s expected to continue to decelerate, reflecting the
convergence of expectations to the official end-2006 target and the modest adjustment in
administered prices expected for 2006. Directors considered that the benign inflation outlook
provides significant scope for further steady easing of the monetary policy stance, but maintaining
the cautious approach adopted by the Central Bank-given          the need to consolidate the gains
against inflation, the uncertainties surrounding the transmission mechanism of monetary policy,
and the risks in the environment. Inthis context, Directors noted the reforms to the credit market
and the improvements in central bank liquidity management that have strengthened monetary
policy, and encouraged the authorities to continue with these reforms. A number of Directors also
suggested that the present favorable macroeconomic conditions provide a good opportunity to
simplify further and reduce reserve requirements, and thus help reduce the high costs of financial
intermediation. Directors welcomed the staffs conclusion that the banlung sector remains sound;
nevertheless,they advised keeping under close monitoring the rapid growth in credit.




                                                                                                  58

Directors commended the authorities for the prudent conduct of fiscal policy in 2005, and
encouraged the authorities to preserve the strong stance of fiscal policy in the period ahead. Most
Directors agreed that the primary fiscal balance should remain the key policy target, and stressed
the importance of maintaining the strong observed performance with regard to the consolidated
primary surplus, in order to maintain the progress toward debt reduction, provide full scope for
monetary policy easing, and protect economic performance from unexpected volatility in 2006.

Directors stressed the importance of lowering the tax burden, simplifying the tax system,
and reducing spending rigidities while continuing to lower public indebtedness. In this regard,
Directors encouraged the government to develop an agenda for comprehensive fiscal reforms. They
noted that the new ceilings on expenditure and revenue, introduced in the 2006 budget guidelines
law, signal the authorities' desire to contain the steady rise in the tax burden and public spending,
while helping to shift expenditure priorities to needed infrastructure and to build a consolidated
fiscal structure for the future. At the same time, some Directors observed that the ceilings could
imply greater complexity in budgetary management. A number of Directors also viewed the
introduction of a countercyclical adjustment inthe 2006 budget guidelines law as premature. A few
Directors, however, saw the mechanism for countercyclical adjustments more favorably, if
implemented with needed safeguards. Directors stressed that a key element in a package of fiscal
reforms would be to increasebudget flexibility, while reducing tax distortions.

Directors commended the authorities' prudent debt management and the buildup of international
reserves, which have contributed to reducing vulnerabilities. They welcomed the progress made in
pre-financing sovereign external needs, improving the structure of public debt, and developing
domestic capital markets-including      with the recent issuance of the real-denominated sovereign
bond and the substantial overall reduction in the public sector's exposure to currency risk. With
reduced macroeconomic volatility and a downward sloping yield curve, Directors felt that
conditions are favorable for a significant improvement in the structure of public debt, and
particularly for further gains in overall debt maturity. Directors encouraged the authorities to
continue their efforts to develop domestic capital markets by further facilitating access to foreign
investors and by phasing out taxes on financial transactions. They also welcomed the authorities'
commitment to continue building up international reserves, while preserving a flexible exchange
rate regime.

Directors commended the authorities for the progress made with their poverty reduction agenda.
They welcomed the evidence that sustained growth, lower inflation, higher formal employment,
and the expansion of social programs have led to a significant improvement in social conditions
and living standards. Directors commended the reduction in the poverty rate and in income
inequality in2004 to their lowest levels since 1992 and 1981, respectively.

Directors urged the authorities to reinvigorate the reform agenda to boost medium-termgrowth and
to help further reduce poverty and inequality. They regretted that the political situation in 2005 has
delayed the government's reform agenda in congress, while they foresee further limitations to
progress in the run-up to the general elections in 2006. In this regard, they encouraged the
authorities to make efforts to advance key reform priorities, including with respect to the
harmonization of the state value added tax system; the establishment of formal central bank
autonomy; the implementation of regulations for complementary pension funds for civil servants;
and steps for further improvement in the business climate.




                                                                                                   59

             ANNEX 5: DETAILED DEBT SUSTAINABILITYANALYSIS

Summary

In 2003, the Minas Gerais state government promoted a strong adjustment program in order to
reverse the unsustainable trend that its fiscal accounts had been taken in the previous period.
Under a program called Choque de Gesta`o (Management Shock), the state government defined a
set of measures directed to curb the increasing trend of expenditures through tight control of
personnel and operating costs. On the revenue side, measures were taken to improve the efficiency
of tax collection.

The results were immediate and impressive. Minas Gerais generated substantial fiscal balances.
The primary balance increased from 4.4% to 7.5% of net current revenue, the current balance
increased from -5% to 2.8% of net current revenue and the nominal balance passedfrom -5.7% to
0.7% of net current revenue. It i s noteworthy that this fiscal turnaround happened in a period of
severe economic stagnation, which resulted in a decrease of 7% in fiscal revenues. Given reduced
revenues, the reduction of expenditures was the only way to improve fiscal balances. Total
expenditures decreased 10%.

In2004 the fiscal adjustment effort of Minas Gerais was deepened. The stategovernment obtained
a vigorous primary surplus of 15.5% of net current revenue, generated current account savings of
14% and generated a nominal balance of 8.6% of net current revenue. Different from the previous
year, the strengthening of the fiscal adjustment was focused on revenue collection. The strong
recovery of the Brazilian and Minas Gerais economies also contributed to the consolidation of the
adjustment, allowing an increase of fiscal revenues of about 12%.

Thus, the combination of the control of current expenditures and the enhanced efficiency in
collection allowed the Minas Gerais government to produce an impressive fiscal turnaround. At
the same time, the reduction of current revenues and the increase of tax revenues enhanced the
government's ability to generate current savings and ledto the recovery of investment expenditures
which would have a positive impact on the growth of the regional economy.

Projection exercises for the period 2005-2014 depict a favorable evolution of the main fiscal and
financial indicators showing that the continuity of the responsible fiscal behavior should guarantee
the debt sustainability. However, the sensitivity analysis shows that the predicted improvement
critically depends on further improvement in efficiency of tax collection and the continuation of
tight control over current expenditures. Additionally, positive prospects depend on the hypothesis
of a higher economic growth (which affects revenue) vis-&vis the population growth (which affects
expendituresj.

Risk analysis shows that the most important source of vulnerability is the high level of
indebtedness. Inparticular, there i s a highprobability that highdebt service will continue to exert a
strong pressure on the state public finances.       This vulnerability indicates the importance of
continuing policies of tight control over expenditures and revenue enhancementwhich are variables
under the government's control.

As for the expected fiscal impact of additional borrowing for the proposed operation, the amount
involved is small relatively to the size of the state in terms of fiscal numbers (debt, revenues and
expenditures), and thus its impact on fiscal balances would also be small. From 2006 to 2014, an




                                                                                                  62

increase in current and primary balances of an average of 3% and of 4% for nominal balance i s
expected.

This report is divided into seven parts. The first describes the evolution of fiscal balances,
revenues and expenditures for the period 2000-2004. The second section analyzes the evolution
and composition of state debt. The third relates to the evolution of the main Fiscal Responsibility
Law indicators of Minas Gerais and the accomplishment of the state fiscal accounts with the legal
ceilings. The fourth part contains the projection exercises which depict scenarios for the evolution
of fiscal accounts and estimate the impact of the World Bank lending operation on the state fiscal
accounts. The fifth section reports on results of a sensitivity analysis to illustrate the effects of
changes in the determinants of fiscal accounts. The sixth section consists of a risk analysis to
verify the consistency of the results obtained in the projection exercises. Finally, the section seven
concludes the report.

A -MINAS      GERAISFISCALSITUATION:           2000-2004

A.l Evolution of FiscalBalances

Minas Gerais emerged from the 1990s facing a very difficult fiscal situation. The combination of
lax fiscal behavior and the tight national monetary policy used for stabilization purposes duringthe
period 1995-98, ledto an unsustainable path for the state fiscal accounts at the end of the decade.

As a result of the Debt Refinancing Agreement signed between the state government and the
National Treasury Secretariat in 1999, Minas Gerais initiated a fiscal adjustment program aimed at
abandoning the unsustainable path that the state debt had followed inthe previous period.40

In2000, the turnaround in the fiscal stance and the economic recovery resulted inthe generation of
substantial fiscal balances. Primary balance achieved 4.4% of net current revenue, the current
account balance was 1.3%, and the nominal deficit was reduced to 4.7%41.

However, the period 2001-2002 saw weakening of this adjustment effort.                        Primary balance
decreased to 0.8% of net current revenue in 2001, although it recovered to 3.7% in 2002. Current
account savings turned negative at -2.8% of net current revenue in 2001 and -5% in 2002. Nominal
deficits increased to almost 10% of net current revenue in 2001 and stayed at 5.7% in 2002.
Additionally, the slowdown of economic growth and the exchange rate depreciation, due to a series
of adverse shocks suffered by the Brazilian economy during this period, led to a resumption
towards increasing state indebtedness.

In 2003, the new state administration launched a strong adjustment program. Under the program
called Choquede GestLio (Management Shock), the government defined a set of measures directed
to curb the increasing trend of expenditures through a tight control over personnel and operating




40The 1997 refinancing agreement between the federal government and state governments was conditioned on
the adoption of Fiscal Adjustment Programs, coordinated by the National Treasury Secretariat. The program
had targets on indebtedness,primary results, personnel expenditures, revenues, investments and privatization.
41Net Current Revenue is the variable used in the Fiscal Responsibility Law to establish limits to expenses,
indebtedness and other fiscal variables. For states, net current revenue consist of the total current revenue, net
of transfers to municipalities, the earmarked revenues for the funding of FUNDEF (education Fund) and state
employee's social security contributions.


                                                                                                               63

costs. Measures were taken on the also revenue side but the economic recession did not allow
significant increases in revenue collection.

The results were immediate and impressive: the primary balance increased to 7.5% of net current
revenue, current balance increased to 2.8%, and nominal balance achieved a positive 0.7%. It i s
noteworthy that this fiscal turnaround happened in a period of severe economic stagnation, which
resulted in a decrease in total revenues of 7.0%.                With reduced revenues, the reduction of
expenditures was the only way to improve fiscal balances. Total expenditures decreasedby 10.0%
at constant prices from 2002 to 2003, with a decrease of 7.0% in current expenditures and 31.O% in
capital expenditures. In this sense, the adjustment of Minas Gerais in 2003 differed from the
similar efforts at the federal government, which were basedon revenue increases.42

In2004 the fiscal adjustmenteffort ofMinasGerais was deepened. The stategovernment obtained
a vigorous primary surplus of 15.5% of net current revenue, generated current account savings of
 14% and generateda nominal balance of 8.6% of net current revenue. Different from the previous
year, the strengthening of the fiscal adjustment was focused on revenue collection. Total revenues
increased by 12.0% at constant prices inthis year, despite a reductionin capital revenues of 21.0%.
Current revenuesincreased 13.0%in2004.43

The recovery of the economic activity in 2004 and the improvement in the efficiency of tax
collection contributed to consolidating the fiscal adjustment. Tax revenues increased 12.4% in
2004 at constant prices. As the estimative for national GDP growth in 2004 is 5%, this represented
a growth 6.7% above nominal GDP.44 Thus, an important part of the tax revenue increaseresulted
from the enhancement of the efficiency on state tax collection.

On the expenditure side, the government maintained the strict control of current expenditures and
achieved significant savings - relative to the projected levels without the adjustment efforts - in
personnel and operating expenditures. With increased revenues, the ability to generate current
savings allowed the Minas Gerais government to finance the recovery of investment expenditures.
Thus, the deepeningof the fiscal adjustment in 2004, basedon revenue increasesand the control of
current expenditures, allowed the recovery of investment expenditures which would have a positive
impact on the growth of the regional economy.45

In summary, the combination of the control of current expenditures and the enhancement of
revenue collection efficiency allowed Minas Gerais to produce an impressive fiscal turnaround of
good quality. At the same time, the strengthening of the control of current expenditures and the
efficiency gains in tax collection, if maintained, would ensure the sustainability of the fiscal
adjustment effort initiated in2003.



42 While the federal government has the constitutional authorities to introduce new taxes and contributions
(and has used this power extensively), state governments are not allowed to create new sources of revenue.
This explains why the federal government tax revenues increased in aperiod of economic slowdown while the
state tax revenues were negatively affected by the stagnation of economic activity during the period 2001-
2003.
43 I t i s worth noticing that even with an increase of total expenditures of 5%, its level i s still 5% below 2001
level at constant prices.
44Minas Gerais State GDP has shown the same evolution as national GDP recently.
45 The impact of the adjustment on expenditure composition constitutes another important difference between
the adjustment of Minas Gerais and of the federal government which, given the difficulties to control current
expenditures, relied on investment expenditures cuts.


                                                                                                                64

The strong fiscal adjustment of the last two years has made it possible that in 2004 the Fiscal
Responsibility Law requirements on debt service and on personnel expenditures would be met.
The same i s expected of the debt level, whose limit would be met from the secondquarter of 2005
onwards.

A.2 Evolution of Fiscal Revenues, 2000-2004.

For the last five years, the trajectory of Minas' fiscal revenues can be divided into two periods.
The first period would be from 2000 to 2003, characterized by low growth performance, and the
other would be 2004 when a strong increase in economic growth was observed (and this trend
appears to be continuing in 2005). From 2000 to 2003 net current revenues increased 6.796, at
constant prices. Brazil's real GDP growth was of 3.8%, indicating 2.8% increase in revenues
above nominal GDP during the three years. In2004, net current revenues increased 13%. During
the first period, tax revenues grew by 10%. Most of the increase was in 2001. But it i s worth
noticing that 2001 was an atypical year, when the government implemented a one-time tax debt
amnesty to collect extraordinary tax revenues. In2004, tax revenues grew by 12.4%.

As mentioned above, the strong revenue growth resulted from the recovery of the level of economic
activity and the improvement of tax collection efficiency. Assuming that Minas Gerais grew at the
same rate as the national GDP in 2004 (Le., 5%), the growth of the state tax revenues at 6.7%
would be above the growth of nominal GDP. Thus a good part of the increase would be due to
improvements in tax collection effort. In 2003, the state government defined thirty one priority
structural projects under the name of "Geraes" Program.46 Among them i s the program of
modernization of the state revenue service, with investment in infrastructure, software, logistic,
modernization of administrative process. In order to increase tax collection, a regime of annual
collection targets and a scheme of incentives to the state employees were introduced.

The most important state tax, the ICMS,47which represented89% of tax revenuein 2004, increased
by 12%. From January to October, the increase of ICMS collection in Minas Gerais was higher
than at the national level for the same tax by 2.6%, which is likely due to the state government's
effort to enhance collection.         EVA4*and the remaining taxes increased by 18% and 15%
respectively. New fee charges were created and the existingfee scheduleswere adjusted.

The same pattern observed for taxes was observed for the current transfers from the federal
government: low growth performance until 2003 and strong recovery in 2004. During the period
2000-2003, federal current transfers fell by 2.6%. If SUS (National Health System) transfers were
not included in 2003, the fall would reach 13%.49 Despite an increase of 14% of the State
Participation Fund (FPE - Fundo de ParticipagZo Estadual), there was a decrease of 44% in PI-
Exp. and 37% in ICMS Compensation from Law 87/9650. Differently, in 2004, federal current
transfers grew by 11% at constant prices. Most of the increase (71%) resulted from the CIDE




46"GestBo EstratCgicados Recursos e A@es do Estado"
47A VAT collected by the states.
48Automobile property tax.
49SUS transfers to Minas Gerais began in 2002. Operation of SUS (National Health System - Sistema Unico
de Sadde) involves a transfer to cover the costs of health assistance provided by the state government, to
implement a national policy of decentralized health provision from federal government to lower levels of
government.
50 FPE i s a revenue sharing mechanism for resources from income tax (IR) and industrialized products tax
(IPI) charged by the state. IPI-Exp i s also a mechanism to share the revenue from the industrialized products
tax to exporter states. ICMS Compensation from Law 87/96 compensates states from the exemption from
ICMS taxation of goods produced for exportation, established by Complementary Law n. 87/96. The amount
of compensation was first established by a specific law, but now i s determined in annual federal budget laws.


                                                                                                            66

 transfer^,^^ which began to be transferred in 2004, and the transfer of SUS with an increase of 40%
at constant prices.

Overall, given the better performance of tax revenues vis-d-vis the federal transfers, the state
dependence on transferred resources was reduced. In 2000, current transfers represented 20.2% of
current revenue while in 2004 the dependence on transfers fell to 17.8%. It i s important to note
that in 2000, the transfers corresponding to the SUS and CIDE did not exist. As in 2004, they
represented 16.9% of current transfers. If these transfers were not included, the dependence on
federal transfers would fall to 15.3%.

As a result, the current revenue composition does not represent a major fiscal risk in the sense that
reductions in intergovernmental transfers do not have a significant impact on Minas Gerais' fiscal
situation.

On the capital account, capital revenues were reduced considerably from 2000 to 2004 - 67% at
constant prices. With the exception of capital transfers, all items strongly fell during this period.
Credit operations were reduced 95%, but have historically been very small in all the years due to
severe limitations on new credit operations imposed by the FiscalAdjustment Program, agreedwith
the National Treasury Secretariat, and by the National Monetary Council controls on credit
supplied by financial institutions to public sector.52 The highest level during this period was in
2000, with 1.5% of net current revenues, well below the Fiscal Responsibility Law ceiling for
credit operations, 16.0% of net current revenues.

After privatization at the end of the nineties, asset sales had reduced its importance as a revenue
source. From R$ 1.2 billions in 2000 (at prices of 2004), it amounted only R$ 29 million in 2003
and R$ 24 million in 2004. Capital transfers showed an irregular pattern since 2000. Froma level
of R$ 146 millions in 2000, it representedR$ 1.2 billions in 2002, decreasingto R$276 millions in
2004. From the R$ 1.2 billion registered in 2002, R$ 1billion was a federal government transfer
due to an agreement where the responsibility for maintenance of some of the federal highways in
Minas Gerais State was transferred to the state government.

Another important component of capital revenue i s debt amortization revenue. These revenues are
from state government funds for development that are managed by the state development bank
(BDMG- Banco de Desenvolvimento de Minas Geruis). Although it declined by 18% from 2000
to 2004 at constant prices, it still represented 53% of capital revenue in 2004.




51 CIDE (Contribui@o de Interven@o no Domini0 EconBmico) is an economic contribution charged over

was created in 2001 (ConstitutionalAmendment n. 33, 2001) and has its revenue collection shared with states
and municipalitiessince 2004.
52NationalMonetary CouncilResolutionsNo. 2827 limit bank exposure to the public sector to 45% of equity.

A.3 Evolution of Expenditures, 2000-2004.

From 2000 to 2004, current expenditures increased by 9.0% at constant prices. In 2001, current
expenditures showed a strong increase of 13.0%, followed by their stagnation in 2002. The
beginningof the fiscal adjustment in 2003 resulted in a reduction of 7.0% while the recovery of
revenues allowed an increase of 3.0% in 2004.           The behavior since 2003 exhibits the new
administration policy of public spending control. The level of current expenditures in 2004 was
still below the 2001 level at constant prices.

Personnel expenditures are the most important component of current expenditures, representing
54% of the total in 2004. From 2000 to 2002, they increased by 10% at constant prices, following
the same pattern of evolution of total current expenditures. In 2003, the government promoted a
strong reduction of personnel expenditures by 10.0%. In2004, there was an increase of 5.0% due
to stagnating growth, new hiring, and some wage adjustments that were postponed in 2003. In any
case, it i s important to mention that the new administration reduced personnel expenditures by 5%
at constant prices.

The fall in personnel expenditures was the result of a set of measures in the Choque de Gest6o
(Management Shock) program, as described in the government's Letter of Development Policy
(Annex 1) and elsewhere in this document. As a result, it was estimated that the monthly nominal
inertial growth of the wage bill was around 0.3% in the beginning of 2003, and now should be
around 0.1596, according to state officials.53 The effective control of personnel expenditures
allowed the state to reduce the Fiscal Responsibility Law indicator of personnel expenditure on net
current expenditures from 66.0% in 2002 to 59.0% in 2004, thus meeting the Fiscal Responsibility
Law requirement on this item.

The second most important component of current expenditure corresponds to operating
expenditures (classified as "other current expenditures"), mainly expenditures for purchases of
goods and services and operation and maintenance. In 2004, the level of these expenditures was
9.0% higher than in 2000 at constant prices. But all of the increases took place from 2000 to 2002,


53Personnelexpenditures here include not only employees but also retirees and pensioners.


                                                                                                69

when they increased 31.0%. From 2002 to 2004, other current expenditures actually fell by 17.0%
(7.0% in 2003 and 11.0% in 2004).

The fall in operating expenditures also reflects the adoption of a series of measures aimed at
improving the public spending control systems.             A new system of services and goods
administration i s being used since January 2004 (SIAP - Sistema de AdministraGZo de Materiais e
ServiGos do Estado de Minus Gerais). This system allows control of the complete contracting
process of goods and services and regulation of the registries of prices and suppliers. Also,
measures were taken to reduce current expenditures like leases of properties and utilities such as
water, electricity and phone.

Interest payments and constitutional transfers to municipalities increased20% and 22% from 2000
to 2004. The transfers to municipalities are determined by the Constitution in such a way that any
tax revenue increase would be translated into increases in transfers to municipalities. As both
interest payments and constitutional transfers are rigid expenditures, their evolutions are out of the
government control. In this sense, if we consider only personnel expenditures and other current
expenditures, the components over which the government has some control, there was an
accumulated reduction of 9%, at constant prices, in 2003 and 2004. This happened in spite of a
high degree of nominal rigidity in personnel expenditures, which makes this achievement even
more significant.

Capital expenditures declined by 28% from 2000 to 2004. Most of this reduction was due to a
decrease in debt amortization (67%) and other capital expenditures (49%). Duringthe same period,
direct investment increased 113%. The increase took place every year with the exception of 2003,
when it fell by 32%. In 2003, the new administration implemented an immediate reduction in less
rigid expenditures, most of which were capital expenditures. But direct investment recovered in
2004 to a level 13% higher than in 2002 thanks to the effect of the initial adjustment efforts. This
allowed an increase in the participation of investment in total expenditures during the period. In
2000, the share of direct investment intotal expenditures was of 2%. This increasedto 5% in2004.
 Debt service has been above the ceiling established by Federal Senate Resolution No.43/2001, in
compliance with the Fiscal Responsibility Law. The legal ceiling is 11.5% often current revenue
and the State has been above this ceiling in all years from 2000 to 2004.

In summary, the evolution of the different expenditure categories shows that the fiscal adjustment
initiated in 2003 is having a positive effect on the quality of expenditures. The reduction in current
expenditures and the strong revenue increase allowed the state to increase the space for investment
expenditures. Over time, the increase in statepublic investment expenditures should allow the state
to overcome the infrastructure bottlenecks that constrained its economic growth, thus favoring the
state's debt sustainability.

In terms to functional allocation, the most important item of the state expenditures corresponds to
education and culture, with 21.5% total primary expenditures in 2003, followed by security
(14.2%) and health and sanitation expenditures (9.5%).          Since 2000, there was a reduction in
education and security expenditures of 4.3% and 1.1% of total expenditures, respectively. At the
same time, there was an increase in spending on social security, health, transport and others.

It is important to notice that the state complied with the constitutional spending floor for basic
education and health in 2003. At the same time, the state government increasedthe basic education
cycle by one year, which impliedan increase in the number of students attending basic education.
This increase did not generate additional spending, showing that improving the provision of public
services can be obtained through efficiency gains without additional expenditures.

B-Evolutionof Consolidated Debt.

From2000 to 2003, consolidated debt increased by 11% at constant prices, in a period where credit
operation amounted to only R$ 178 millions at constant prices of 2004. Most of the increase (78%)
was due to the evolution of the state debt with the Federal Government, which represented90% of
the consolidated debt stock in 2003. The origin of this debt was refinancing agreements between
federal government and state government^.^^

The last refinancing agreement between Minas Gerais and the National Treasury was done under
the Law No. 9496/97. It amounted to R$ 12.9 billion or 16% of state GDP, representing 84% of
the state debt with the National Treasury and 80% of the state's total debt.

The agreement under Law No.9496/97 was conditional on the adoption of the Fiscal Adjustment
Program, supervised by the National Treasury Secretariat. The program established targets on
indebtedness, primary balances, personnel expenditures, revenues, investments and privatization.
For the last revision of the agreement in 2004, Minas Gerais had achieved all the targets
established, with the exception of the target corresponding to assets sales. Even then, the State was
considered by the National Treasury as fulfilling the debt renegotiation contract, without any
penalty to the State.

The increase in the state indebtednesswith the federal government has two main causes. The first
i s the index used to correct the debt stock: the General Price Index (IGP). This index i s much more
influenced by exchange rate changes than consumer price indexes. While there was an exchange



54 Brazil's federal government set up three bailout operations in ten years, reflectingthe weak fiscal discipline
of state governments. In 1989 the federal government assumed R$ 10.5 billion of state's external debt which
represented 1.4% of GDP. In 1993, the National treasury assumed R$ 40 bi or 7.2% of GDP of state's debt
with federal financial institutions.Finally, in 1997, the federal government restructured state's bond debt by
R$87 bi or 11.7%of GDP. (for more detailedinformation, see Bevilaqua, 1999)


                                                                                                             72

rate devaluation of 48% from December 2000 to December 2003, the General Price Index during
this period showed a variation of SO% andthe consumer price index -IPCA - varied by 32%.

The other cause i s the ceiling on debt service. Debt service fromthe refinancingagreement and set
of contracts also set in the agreement should be below 13% of net real revenue.55Any debt service
above this limit i s automatically incorporated into, and thus increases,the debt stock. This explains
why, even inthe absence of large new credit operations, the debt stock has grown.

Another component of the state debt i s the debt with CEMIG, the public electricity company with
the state government controlling 51% of the voting shares, which also showed a significant increase
during the period (41%, or 906 millions of 2003 Reais). This debt is under renegotiation and
interests have not being paid in excess of dividends received by the state.

Finally, external debt was reduced during the period, despite devaluation of the Real. This is due
to amortizations done duringthe period and the absence of new credit operations since 1999.

The Federal Senate Resolution40/2001, complying with the Fiscal Responsibility Law, established
a ceiling for net consolidated debt to net current revenues of 200% for state governments. For
states that were above this ceiling, the Resolution mandated an adjustment to the ceiling in fifteen
years. In 2002, Minas Gerais was above the ceiling established by the adjustment path, as the high
depreciation and inflation measured by the general price index - as discussed above - caused a
considerable increase in state debt stocks.

As a result, the Senate Resolution 20/2003 exempted states and municipalities from fulfilling the
legal ceiling from January 2003 to April 200.5. Numbers from the Minas Gerais Fiscal Report of
August (Relatdrio de Gestiio               showed that at this time the State was only 0.43% above the
ceiling established by the path adjustment. It i s expected that this limit will be met in December
2004.

revenues.

Interms of its composition, in2003,90.3% of the debt stock from Minas Gerais was indexedto the
General Price Index (IGP) and 9.5% to the exchange rate. As the general price index i s very
sensitive to changes on exchange rate, debt stock i s influenced by changes in the exchange rate.
Thus, the exchange rate constitutes the most relevant risk for debt sustainability as almost 100% of
the state debt i s indexed directly or indirectly to the exchange rate. This fact reveals that an
additional external credit operation will not generate additional exchange rate vulnerability. The
exchange rate risk will be analyzed in more detail in sections E and F on sensitivity and risk
analyses.

C -Compliance with the FiscalResponsibility Law

With the exception of the requirement on credit operations, it is clear that Minas Gerais did not
meet the Fiscal Responsibility Law key indicator requirements since its enactment in 2000. But it
i s important to notice that the adjustments made in the last 2 years, with expenditures control and
revenue enhancing, led to the compliance with the LRF requirements on debt services and on
personnel expenditures in 2004, as shown in Table 8. The same is expected of the debt level,
whose limit has to fall within the adjustment path from the secondquarter of 2005 onwards.

D-Projected FiscalSituation: 2005 -2014

In this section, Minas Gerais State fiscal situation will be projected in order to assess the state's
capacity to repay with regard to the proposed lending operation and its fiscal impact. For this, two
scenarios will be depicted: first without the lending operation and second with the World Bank
lending operation.

The projection will look at the evolution of current, primary and nominal balances and the
compliance with the Fiscal Responsibility Law indicators.            Besides these figures, other two
indicators will be analyzed to assess the state's cash flow. The first i s interest coverage, which
represents current account cash flow without interest payments (flow of funds i s generated
internally) divided by the interest payment. The minimumlevel recommended for this indicator is
1.5. The second i s investment coverage, which represents the amount of investment financed with
cash flow (current account balance). The minimumlevel recommended for this indicator is 30%.

The main hypotheses for both projections are presented in Table 9 below.                   The market
expectations, based on the Central Bank Report "Market Readout," were used to set values for
inflation, GDP growth and exchange rate in these exercise^.'^ The level of investment from 2005
afterwards is set as equal to the average from 2000 - 2003, adjusted by inflation. The simulation
considers new credit operations when total balance i s not enough to finance current and capital
expenditures.




57The expectation was from the December 30, 2004.

  December 30,2004.

  Firstscenario: without the World Banklendingoperation

  This scenario projects the fiscal situation of Minas Gerais without the World Bank lending
  operation. The results are presented in Tables 10 and 11 below. All the balances are positive
  during the period estimated and increasing as percentage of net current revenue. In 2014, the
  current balance would achieve 21% of net current revenue, and the primary and nominal balances
  22% and 18%, respectively.

  Although the gross consolidated debt will increase duringthis period, there is a big reductionin the
  net consolidated debt because of the assumption that total savings will be accumulated and not
  spent. The estimation shows that the legal path for debt reduction will be accomplished every


                                                                                                              76

year.58 But this only happens because it was assumed that savings were not spent. If they were
totally allocated to investment, for instance, although debt to net consolidated level would decrease,
it would not be sufficient to guaranteethe compliance with the legalceiling each year.

The ceiling for personnel expenditures (60% of net current revenues) will also be achieved every
year in the projection even though Minas Gerais did not meet requirements on consolidated debt
and personnel expenditures until 2003.

The other two limits established by the Fiscal Responsibility Law are the ceilings for credit
operations and the debt service, both as percentages of net current revenue. As there are positive
savings every year and thus no need for additional credit operations, the limit on annual credit
operations will not be relevant. For debt service, the legal ceiling i s 11.5%. The projection shows
that the state will be above in all years, although showing a slightly decreasing ratio. But this
would happen only if the financial assets accumulated would not be used to amortize debt. The
increase in this indicator in relation to 2004 is probably due to the fact that our projections consider
the debt service of CEMIG debt, of R$ 2.2 billions in 2003. As mentioned before, this contract is
being renegotiated and the state government has not been paying all its debt service in the last
years.

For the other indicators considered, interest coverage and investment coverage, the projection
exercise shows that both will be above the minimumlevels recommended during the period 2005-
2014.

It is important to mention that the projected improvement in fiscal balances for the coming years
are due to hypotheses considered: some items of the revenues depend on economic growth while
important components of expenditures are influenced by population growth. As our hypothesis of
the economic growth i s higher than the estimated population growth, the estimation predicted a
better fiscal situation in the future. An analysis of the sensibility of the projection to economic
growth will be done inthe section E.




58 Federal Senate Resolution n. 40/2001, as determined by Fiscal Responsibility Law, established limits for
state indebtedness. The ceiling is of 200% of net current revenue. For states that were above this level, it was
given a 15 year period to reach this level, with a reduction of 1/15 each year. It was the case of Minas Gerais,
which net debt was 234% of net current revenue at 2001. Inthis sense, each year, the level of indebtednesshas
to decrease by 2.3% of net current revenue, achieving 200% in 2016.

Second Scenario: with World Bank lendingoperation

Inthis scenario, the projection exercise considers the effects on debt, revenues and expenditures of
World Banking lending operation of R$ 510 millions for general budget support (i.e., not
earmarked to specific spending purposes).              Furthermore, it assumes that additional budget
resources that the Bank operation would release for the government to fully fund programs directed
to improve the fiscal equilibrium and provision of public service as well as promote economic
growth. These include programs for revenue and financial administration, planning, budget, supply
and personnel management, electronic government, debt amortization, citizen security, public
infrastructure investments and public-private partnerships project^.'^ Details of the application of
resources and the potential fiscal savings that each project would generate are shown on Box 4
below.

Box 4: Assumptions regarding the use off additional budget resources

The application of resources from the World Bank lending operation within different projects and the
projected fiscal gains are described below. Table 12 below shows a summary of the different government
actions. The projections of fiscal gains were done by the state government and were described in the Policy
Letter sent to the Bank.

To strengthen revenue administration, R$50 million would be allocated to finance investment in additional
infrastructure (e.g., hardware and software). The government has already invested in revenue collection with
results that can be observed in 2004. This project i s expected to generate additional tax collection of R$44.4
million of 2005 Reais from 2007 on. For financial management, an investment of R$10 i s planned in
software, hardware and staff capacity building. An expected return i s an annual reduction of expenditures by
R$4.4 million of 2005 Reais (R$3 million from more efficient data processing and R$1.4 million from
collection of supplier interest payments and fines that a more efficient financial managementwould allow) and
an annual increase of interest revenues due to better cash flow management of R$2.3 millions of 2005 Reais
from 2007 on.

For strengthening planning capacity, the government i s planning investments of R$5 millions, from which a
return of R$9.3 millions is expected from 2006 on, which would represent rationalization of 3.0% of the
investments in that year. Another R $ l million will be applied to the public management by the results
program.

Personnel management would benefit from an investment of R$8 million, in addition to the considerable
amount of measures the state has already implemented to allow for better control of personnel payment,
reduction of irregular payment as well as alleviation of stagnant growth. Additional Bank resources would be
used to improve the personnel administration system, SISAP, and to implement a new system of personnel
payment integrated to it. The return expected from this investment i s a reduction in personnel expenses of
R$4.3 millions of 2005 Reais from 2007 on. Also for personnel policy management, an investment in
employees training worth R$10 millions is considered. As a result, expected savings in personnel outlays
would reach R$2.3 millions of 2005 Reais from 2007 on, with a reduction of 300 contracted employees; and a
reductioningoods and services expenditures of R$ 3.04 million from 2007 on.

The state government has implemented a new system of services and goods administration (SIAP -Sistema de
4dministra@o de Materiais e ServiGos do Estado de Minus Gerais). This system allows control of the
zomplete contracting process of goods and services as well as regulation of the price and supplier registry
systems. With the proposed DPL's general budget support, the government would be able to allocate


59The proposed DPL would not directly finance these programs. The DPL would support some of the policies
of which some of these programs form part, but the programs mentioned here also include those that lie
outside the programmatic support of the proposed DPL (e.g., citizen security, infrastructure investments).


                                                                                                            80

additional R$8 million to finance the complete implementation of SIAD, which is expected to lead to a
reduction in goods and services outlays of R$4.8 millions of 2005 Reais from 2007 on.

The implementation of the electronic government initiative would absorb R$15 million with the following
fiscal impacts: reduction in telephone bills (R$2.6 million from 2006 on), reduction of maintenance
expenditures of the systems that will be part of the e-government initiative (R$0.69 millions from 2007
onwards) and reduction in paper acquisition (R$0.7 millions from 2007 onwards).

Inthe process of implementing a new managementmodel, the government introduced a new legal framework
to foster partnership between the government and civil society organizations and the private sector.
Partnerships with civil society organizations will be operationalized through the OSCIP model (Organizap5o
da Sociedade Civil de Interesse Pliblico) and its partnership with the state government, whose implementation
i s expected to consume R$ 1 million of the additional budget resources. For the private sector-government
partnership, a framework for public-private partnerships (PPP) i s being implemented, directed to promote
investments and economic growth. Implementation of these operations would require R$lOO million of
additional resources to capitalize a PPP guarantee fund (or an equivalent mechanism). The implementation of
the two first PPPs operations (five pilot-projects were already defined) would result in government saving of
R$20 million from 2007 to 2016.

Also with the aim of inducing private investment, R$40 million would be spent for infrastructure investment in
road maintenance and in support of the "Estrada Real" project. Estrada Real is an important project with the
aim of enhancing tourism in the state's historic cities. The projected fiscal impact is shown inTable 12 below.

Another planned investment activity i s an R$lOO-million investment in citizen security with fiscal gain of
R$60.77, R$60.09 and R$27.04 millions in 2006, 2007 and 2008 respectively.

Some of the resources are going to be used for debt amortization: R$51 million to contracts indexed by TR
and with 12% interest rates and R$16 million to contracts indexed by IGP-M and 3% interest rates. Both
contracts have a high level of amortization in the next five years (79% for the TR indexed contracts and 100%
of the IGP-M indexed contracts). In this way, its payment will decreasethe debt service expected for the next
years.

Similarly, R$95 million would be used to retire some of the judicial debts (precatdrios). This debt i s
corrected by 12% year plus the INPC (National Consumer Price Index). Inthis sense, its early payment would
represent savings of fiscal resources over time. But it i s important to mention that this cannot be easily seen in
the fiscal balances. First of all, in this exercise, the level of judicial debt is computed by historical levels,
which may be very different from the actual ones. Inthis sense, the reduction on balances would be less than
R$ 95 millions paid (although it will be computed as expenses). Also, there is not any interest payment so the
implicit reduction in debt service i s not going to be detected in financial sheets.

E Sensitivity Analysis
  -
Using the World Bank lending operation as the baseline, a sensitivity analysis exercise was
performed. The purpose was to identify the most important risks to future financial performance of
the Minas Gerais state government. The analysis i s based on a set of potential risks considered
most important and assesses the state's financial performance sensitiveness to each of them.
Changes in revenues (tax, social contribution and current transfers) and expenditures (personnel
and others current expenditures - without interest and constitutional transfers) will be considered
as well as changes in the most important economic determinants of fiscal sustainability, economic
growth, and exchange rate.

In the previous section, there were six financial indicators used to analyze the financial health of
the state: the four indicators set by the Fiscal Responsibility Law (ceilings for debt level, debt
service, credit operations and personnel expenditures), plus interest and investment coverage. Of
these indicators, interest coverage, investment coverage, and credit operations will be excluded in
the sensitivity analysis, as the projection exercise showed comfortable situations for these
variables. Also, debt service to net current revenue will not be considered as it is already above the
ceiling defined by the LRF and it is clear that negative developments in its determinants will
increase the distance between this ratio and the LRFceiling. In this sense, the sensitivity analysis
will be focused on the other two remainingindicators: the ratios of debt and personnel expenditures
to net current revenues.

As shown in the previous section, only in 2004 the state beganto comply with the LRFceiling for
these two ratios. Initially, it is important to anticipate that there are high potential financial risks
for Minas Gerais in revenues, expenditures, and in the economic assumptions. Small variations in
each of these variables are sufficient to prevent the government from achieving the legal limits
considered. In particular, the analysis shows that the debt to net current revenue ratio is more
sensitive to changes inthe main variables than personnel expenditures.

On the revenue side, the most important risk i s tax revenues, as it represented67% of total current
transfers in 2003 and 2004. On the expenditure side, personnel expenditures are the major source
of risk, especially the state employees' social security imbalances which represent a real and
substantial source of risk for non-compliance with the LRF requirements. In this sense, programs
that are in progress in the state to increase revenue collection and to exercise a better control over
expenditures, particular personnel outlays, are crucial for the continuing fulfillment of the legal
requirements.

Exchange rate variations are also a major source of risk as almost all of the stock of debt i s
influenceddirectly or indirectly (through the general price index) by the exchange rate.

The projection exercise in the previous section depicted an improvement in the financial situation
during the period analyzed. However, this improvement i s the result of the hypothesis of higher
economic growth (which affects revenue) vis-&-vis the population growth (which affects
expenditures). In this sense, even if a negative development forces the state to fail to comply with
the legal requirements for a few years, the assumption about GDP and population growth rates will
guaranteethe return to a sustainable path.

This positive scenario is very sensitive to the hypothesis about economic growth. Inparticular, an
annual economic growth higher than 1.7% i s necessaryfor the debt path not to be explosive. Inthis
way, changes inthis hypothesis may change our results of fiscal sustainability in the longrun.


                                                                                                     85

i) Revenues

The debt level indicator (net consolidated level to net current revenue ratio) is very sensitive to
changes in revenues, as it depends directly on the latter. Since the debt level is very near to the
ceiling in the initial years, small variations in revenue can hinder meeting the legal requirement.
For example, a 2% decrease in tax revenue is already enough to prevent the state from complying
with the debt ceiling. This shows us that tax revenue i s an important source of risk for the state. In
this sense, revenue administration programs pursued by the state are crucial for its finances.

For social contributions, a decrease of 20% would be necessary before their performance begins to
affect the state's compliance with the debt ceiling. Although this is a higher number, a possibility
for charging compulsory contributions from public employees to provide health assistanceis under
discussion at the Federal Supreme Court. As contribution to health assistance represented an
average of 22.6% of the total social contributions collection in 2003 and 2004, we can point social
contributions also as another important risk for Minas Gerais financial situation.

At last, a decrease of 6% of current transfers would imply non-compliance with the debt ceiling.
However, 70% of the current transfers are constitutional, which makes them more stable and less
risky. Of the other current transfers, 21% are from two federal programs, FUNDEF(7%) and SUS
(14%), which we expect will be maintained for the following years. However, the state is only an
intermediary for the SUS system. In this sense, a reduction in the level of transfers should
represent also a reduction in the level of expenditures. But as SUS is a component of net current
revenue, its reduction still has a direct effect on the Fiscal Responsibility Law indicators
requirements.

The legal ceiling for personnel expenditures to net current revenue ratio (60% of net current
revenue) is also very sensitive to revenues, particularly to tax revenue. A reduction of 5% in tax
revenue would be enough for non-compliance with the Fiscal Responsibility Law limit. For current
transfers, this number is 13%, showing less vulnerability. The sensitivity to social contributions, in
turn, is very small, as it would take a reduction of 99% for the risk of non-compliance with the
legal limit for personnel expenditures.

ii) Expenditures

On the expenditures side, two items are considered: personnel expenditures and other current
expenditures, excluding interests and constitutional transfers to municipalities. The state exercises
more control on the former items than the latter, which is constitutional and automatic. Interest
payments for debts already contracted are also outside the state's immediate control. Besides these
rigid expenditure categories, personnel expenditures constitute a substantial source of nominal
rigidity.

Legal ceilings for personnel expenditures and debt level are both very sensitive to changes in
personnel expenditures. An increase of 3% in personnel expenditures is already enough for non-
compliance with the legal ceiling for personnel expenditures. An increase of 4% in personnel
expenditures would place the state at above the legal debt ceiling. This high sensitivity of the legal
indicators to personnel expenditures indicates the importance of state policies directed to personnel
expenditures control.




                                                                                                     86

Imbalance in the state's social security system (only covering retired state public servants) is also
an important source of risk for personnel expenditures. The state's social security system for
government employees is composed of two funds: the FUNPENG (Fundo de Previd2ncia do
Sewidor Pziblico de Minas Gerais) and the FUNFIP(Fundo Financeiro de Previdgncia). The first
one covers new employees (contracted from 2002 on) and the secondone the remainingemployees.
FUNPENG, as a new fund, with no benefit already granted, had an actuarial surplus of R$ 0.8
million, as of the end of 2003. At the same time, the actuarial deficit of FUNFIP was R$51.2
billion. FUNFIP i s a financial fund, which presents an annual social security deficit. The state
government treasury is responsible for transferring the necessary financial resources that guarantee
the payment of pension and retirement benefits. Therefore, social security debt amortization was
already considered in financial balances. Even then, given the large actuarial deficit we should
expect an increase in the FUNFIP's financial needs at a higher rate than the population growth (as
considered inthe projection baseline scenario). Inthis sense, we classified personnel costs variable
of highrisk to Minas Gerais' financial situation.

The sensitivity to other current expenditures i s smaller, as it would take an increase of 11%for the
state to fail to comply with the legal debt ceiling.

iii) EconomicGrowth

As mentioned above, outcomes of the projection exercise depend critically on our assumptions
regarding economic growth. As growth has a direct impact on revenues while population growth
has a direct effect on expenditures, the hypothesis of an economic growth higher than population
growth i s crucial for the projected improvement of the fiscal balances in the future. This section
analyzes sensitivity of the state's public finances to economic growth.

An annual economic growth 0.8% lower than the original hypothesis is sufficient to prevent the
state from complying with the legal debt ceiling. In other words, if economic growth would be of
2.7% in 2005 and 2.2% from then on, the state would not be able to fulfill the Fiscal Responsibility
Law indebtedness requirement. It i s important to remember that Federal Senate Resolution n.40
established a decreasing path for debt level for states above the LRF ceiling of 200% of net current
revenue. In other words economic growth of 0.8% under the original hypothesis implies non-
compliance with the declining path defined by the Resolution 40, but it does not imply an increase
inthe debt level over time, or an explosivepath. An unsustainable fiscal path would result from an
economic growth rate of 1.3% or lower (Le., 2.2% in 2005 and 1.7% from then on).

Meeting the personnel expenditures ceiling i s also sensitive to economic growth, but to a lesser
degree. The state's personnel expenditure to net current revenue ratio would fall below the 60%
mark as defined by the LRF if economic growth were 1.8% below the assumed level for this
projection exercise.

iv)      Exchange rate

Minas Gerais' debt i s strongly influenced by exchange rate variations: 9.5% of its debt stock in
2003 was indexed to the dollar and 90.3% was indexed to the general price index (IGP), a price
index very sensitive to exchange rate. As a result, a 4% devaluation of the exchange rate would
imply non-compliance with the legal debt ceiling. For this calculation, we assumed that 50%
devaluation would have a direct impact on the general price index. Inthis sense, the achievement
of the legal debt requirement is very sensitive to the small variations inthe exchange rate.



                                                                                                   87

As Figure 7 shows this effect i s on the short run. In other words, a devaluation of 10%would lead
to noncompliance with the debt ceiling for only two years in the projection. After that, the net debt
to net current revenue would continue to fall, complying with the legal requirement. Thus, a
recurrent exchange rate shock would be necessary to prevent a sustainable path for Minas' public
debt.

F-Riskanalysis

Besides the sensitivity analysis for each variable, risk analyses were conducted, considering
simultaneous random shocks ina set of variables and their impacts on the state's financial situation.

To do this analysis, random error was added to each of the following variables: tax revenues,
federal government transfers, state government transfers, personnel expenditures and social
security contributions, other current expenditures (including goods and services), and exchange
rate. For each variable, the random error affected the simulation inthe following way:




where:
xt : variable at the time t;
xt-1: variable at t-1;
gxt: growth rate of the variable x at time t on the base case scenario;

Et: randomerror


For all variables, the assumption was normal distributions with zero mean for all random errors.
For the exchange rate the standard deviation was of 10%. Exchange rate errors will impact dollar
indexed debt and general price index (IGP) indexed debt. The hypothesis is that 50% of exchange


                                                                                                  88

 rate variation has a direct impact on general price index. For other current expenditures and
 personnel expenditures, the standard deviation was 3% and for the current revenues and transfers
 the standard deviation was 5%.        The lower standard deviation for expenditures i s based on the
 hypothesis that the state has more control over these variables. These assumptions are shown on
 Table 15. The model recalculated the financial projection based on a simulation of 1,000 trials.
 More information about the model presentedin Appendix I.

 Indebtedness seems to be the most important issue for the government, mainly due to debt service
 payments. As shown in Table 16 below, the most critical variable is debt service to net current
 revenue ratio, as already discussed above. The probability of compliance with the legal ceiling of
 11.5% for this variable is only of 1%. In our base case scenario this variable was not complied
 with in any of the years projected, although it showed a slightly decreasing pattern. At the same
 time, the ceiling for the indebtedness level i s achieved with probability of 63%. Although a much
 better figure, it indicates that the probability of non-compliance with this ceiling i s considerable.

 The probability of compliance with personnel expenditures ceiling i s 74%. Although the numbers
 showed a significant probability of non-compliance for indebtedness and personnel expenditures, it
 i s worth remembering that until 2003, these limits were not complied with by the state government.
 For interest coverage and investment coverage, indicators that try to evaluate the state's ability to
 generate positive cash flows, the result i s better.       The probability of meeting the established
 threshold is 94% for the interest coverage indicator and 97% for the investment coverage indicator.

G Final Remarks
   -

The Government of the State of Minas Gerais has gone through an impressive fiscal adjustment in
the last two years, with reduction in expenditures and healthy increasesin revenue collection. As a
result, the state government presented better figures for primary, nominal and current surpluses
(respectively 15.5%, 8.6% and 14% of net current revenue) in 2004. This made it possible for the
state to comply with all the legal limits established by Fiscal Responsibility Law by the end of
2004. It i s worth noticing that at the end of 2003 three of the four ceilings were not complied with:
debt level, debt service expenses and personnel expenditures.

For the coming years it is expected that the state will continue to comply with all legal limits (with
the exception of the debt service ceiling) and also a significant improvement in balances obtained.
But this projection is based on two important assumptions: that economic growth will remain
higher than population growth and that the state government does not spend the savings
accumulated during the next years. A higher economic growth would allow a higher rate of
increase in revenues than expenditures, which, according to the assumptions used in the projection,
depend mostly on population growth. Annual economic growth of 1.7% instead of 3% is already
sufficient to create an unsustainable trend for the state's debt. Allocation of the savings resulting
from total balance surpluses to finance additional expenditures would also prevent the state from
complying with debt level ceiling.

The sensitivity analysis also showed highvulnerability. Small variations in revenues, expenditures
and exchange rate level would be enough to prevent the compliance with legal limits. The most
important source of vulnerability is the high level of indebtedness itself.             But personnel
expenditures also contribute to a high risk since an increase inthe social security imbalance, and as
a result, and increase inthe state treasury social security spending are expected

This high vulnerability indicates the importance of continuing policies of tight control over
expenditures and revenue enhancing. The government could allocate additional budget resources
made available as a result of the general budget support of the proposed DPL to finance many of
the projects already in progress that have been responsible for the state financial improvement. As
the amount of the proposed Bank loan (R$510 million, or US$170 million at the exchange rate of
R$3/US$) is relatively small to the total size of the state in terms of fiscal numbers (debt, revenues
and expenditures), its impact on fiscal balances would also be small.




                                                                                                    90
