               ANNEX 6: MINAS GERAISPPPLAW AND REGULATION

Publicationof the State of Minas Gerais (Translation):
Public-PrivatePartnershipsinMinas Gerais September,2005

Introduction

Minas Gerais i s the most advanced state of the country in regards to the preparation to make use of
the public-private partnerships - PPPs. Law Number 14.868, signed by the state governor on
December 14, 2003, was the first tool of such nature in Brazil. In Minas Gerais, the management
structures are already operating, the guarantee mechanisms are being studied and the first projects'
moldings have already been started.

The state's advanced stance has drawn the interest of the Inter-American Bank - LDB. The Bank
madefund-purdue resources available so as to support the PPP Unit of Minas Gerais in developing
the moldings for the piloting projects, for creating the guarantee mechanismsand for disclosingthe
partnership model.      This was the Bank's first financial allocation for a PPP program in any
Brazilian state.

          `` The implementation of the PPP Program in Minas Gerais is quite an innovative
          initiative as it will generate conditions of credibility for an effective relationship between
          the state and the private sector in the provision of public services and infrastructure. The
          program's successful implementation will serve as reference for similar initiatives in
          other state,?.''
          Inter-AmericanDevelopmentBank, in a 2003 documentjustifying the Bank's support to the Minas
          Geraisprogram.

Importancefor the State's Sustainable Development PPAG2004 2007
                                                           -               -
The Pluriannual Plan for Government Action (Plano Plurianual de Apio Governamental - PPAG
2004-2007) reflects the strategic orientation of the state's government, especially as regards the
priorities pronounced by the government in May of 2003. Among such priorities, let us highlight
the following -- "to make new means offinancing undertakings viable by building a new legal mark
focused on public-private partnerships." For this, the PPAG's priorities include actions such as the
structuring of the PPP Program, the forming of a management system and the elaboration of the
first projects - all of which are already taking place inMinas Gerais.

Making the PPP's Program viable shall not be seen as an end to itself, but instead as a means
through which the state can reach its true main priorities that include - to substantially improve
                                                                              "
the security of Minas Gerais' population (...); provide the infrastructure required by Minas Gerais
with emphasis placed on the enlargement and improvement of the roads network and basic
sanitation (...); improvement and increase of services to citizens by rendering quality public
services, especially as pertains to education, health and housing (...); fomenting the state's
economic development (...)and reducing regional inequalities."

It i s demands such as the fore-mentioned ones that the PPP Programwill start to answer to, and the
contributions they will make will not be small. Once the investments and resulting offer of services
gradually begin to be carried out by the private sector, the impacts of the disbursement of public
resourcescan be diluted over longer periods of time.




                                                                                                     96

                                    "Some time ago, we witnessed a time during which the state built a
                          motor vehiclefactory in partnership with Fiat, and also the Hotel Grande
                          de Araxd and an iron and steel factory. Nowadays, the state doesn't even
                          have the right to neglect thinking about placing priority on public security,
                          education and health so as to attenuate areas that are of the private
                          initiative's exclusive responsibility.   Nowadays, we are tracking in the
                          opposite direction of those times - we are bringing the private initiative
                          closer to us. We want the private initiative to be a growing tool, as the
                          state has been, to ensure the development of Minas Gerais in areas where
                          we still have great demands and needs."

                                   - Pronouncement of Governor ACcio Neves upon sanctioning the
                          laws that gives a start to the implantation of the Public-Private
                          Partnerships, on December 16,2003.

Minas Geraisis to be the First Brazilian State to Make Use of a PPP

It is expected that in 2005 Minas Gerais will have the first procured PPP inBrazil. The legislation
of Minas Gerais was the first to be enacted, and allowed the state to move ahead of the rest of the
country in the structuring of the essential management so as for the PPPs to be efficaciously and
securely established.

The Legislationof Minas Gerais-State Laws 14.868 and 14.869 of December 16,2003

In its first lines, the PPPLaw of Minas Gerais states the parameters that were also adoptedby the
Federal Law. The themes and solutions proposed for the implementation of a PPP culture are
present in both legislations. For the concession of guarantees to the PPP contracts, the Law of
Minas Gerais foresees the possibility of creating fiduciary funds, as well as the participation of
state-owned company - CODEMIG, as the contracting party and provider of assets designatedas a
guaranteeof payment to the private sector.

The difference i s that the Law of Minas Gerais i s more explicit and restrictivethan the Federal Law
and the Law of SBo Paulo, as it details exactly what can and cannot be a PPP. In addition, for a
PPP to be established in Minas Gerais, the project must be part of the State Plan for Public-Private
Partnerships, elaborated by Management Council and approved by the Governor of the state.

As the legislators of Minas understand that PPPcontracts should only be used in special situations,
they approved a law that lists cases that cannot be considered as PPP. Such cases include:
outsourcing labor that i s the sole object of a contract; isolated rendering of a service that does not
involve a set of activities, as well as a concession or permission contract whose term is of under
five years or R$ 20 million. Such care in the Law of Minas Gerais reflects the understanding that
banalizes the PPP tool would generate a serious risk of committing a substantial parcel of future
budgets.

Some other aspects of the Law of Minas Gerais:


     0   It does not create a PPP contract as such, as the constitutional competence for this belongs
         to the Union. The state law incentives and makes it possible for partnerships to be
         established by means of existing contractual forms (procurement processes / concessions).
         So, in this sense, it is perfectly compatible with the legislation institutedby the Union.


                                                                                                    97

    0   It is more analytical as per the competenciesof the Executive branch in approvingprojects.
        It specifies that PPPs can be developed in areas pertaining to education, health, social
        assistance; public transportation; basic sanitation; security, the penitentiary system, defense
        and justice; science, research and technology; agribusiness, and other areas of public or
        economic interest.

    0   It specifically voids any PPP that grants the private partner: power to edit any legal acts
        founded on power of authority of public nature; attributions of political, police, legal,
        normative and regulatory nature; attributions pertainingto the executive direction of public
        organizations and entities; and education activities that involve the pedagogical process.

    0   Foresees the annual elaboration of the State Plan for Public-Private Partnerships.

    0   Requires that the technical studies that precede a PPP clearly show the economic and
        operational advantage of the proposal to the state and the improvement in the efficiency in
        employing public resources, as related to other possibilities for the state to carry out the
        service;
        Observation: This list i s illustrative and selective and does not represent the full text of
        Law 14.868/03


Governance: The Management Council,the PPPUnitandthe PPPNetworkof Minas Gerais

The government of Minas Gerais understands that as the PPPs represent an involvement of future
governments and the use of public resources, there must be strict criteria for the processes
pertaining to their selection, evaluation, contracting and fiscalization.       For such, a structure
composed of the main elements listed below was set up:


    0   Management Council for Public-PrivatePartnerships (Conselho Gestor de Parcerias
        PBbZico-Privadas CGP). This council is responsible for elaborating the State Plan for
                           -
        Public-Private Partnerships and for approving the procurement documents, contracts and
        their amendments and prorogations. The CGP i s headed by the governor of the state, and
        its set members are the state's Attorney-General, the State Secretaries of Economic
        Development, Planning and Management, Finances, and of Transportation and Public
        Works, of Regional Development and Urban Policies, and of the Environment and
        Sustainable Development. The head of the secretariat that is directly associated to the
        service or activity that i s the object of the public-private partnership will also work as a
        member of the council.

    0   PPP Unit. The PPP unit is inserted in the scope of the Sub-secretariat for International
        Matters (Subsecretaria de Assuntos Internacionais - SEAIN) and of the State Secretariat of
        Economic Development (Secretaria de Estado de Desenvolvimento Econdmico - SEDE).
        It was created by means of Law Number 14.868/03 and is responsible for executing the
        operational and PPP coordination activities, to advise the CGP, and to disclose the
        concepts and methodologies that are unique to public-private partnership contracts. As
        such, it was consolidated as a Center of Reference on knowledge concerning PPPs. A
        sectorial operational unit will be set up within each organization or entity in which there i s
        potential for partnerships to be carried out, and this unit will be technically linked to the
        central unit. As the PPP contract i s quite complex and requires various studies as per the
        definition of the moldings, the costs for its elaboration is quite high. The PPP unit will also
        serve to minimize this cost as it will centralize knowledge on how to structure projects and




                                                                                                     98

         moldings, how to simplify contracting procedures and make them more transparent, and it
         can even provide advisory services to other public entities.

    0    PPP Network. The PPP network is formed by the entities of the State's Public
         Administration that are involved with the PPPs. It is, above all, a network of intelligence
         and knowledge: there are tens of key-persons within its respective organizations that are
         virtually linked. Inaddition to a central unit, the PPP network currently includes a sectorial
         unit of the State Secretariat of Planning and Management (Secretaria de Estado de
         Planejamentoe GestZo - SEPLAG),of the State Secretariat for Social Defense (Secretaria
         de Estudo de Defesa Social    - SEDS), of the State Secretariat for the Environment and
         Sustainable Development (SEMAD), of the Department of Roads and Highways of Minas
         Gerais (Departamento de Estradas de Rodagem de Minus Gerais          -  DER / MG), of the
         State University of Minas Gerais (UniversidadeEstadual de Minus Gerais - UEMG), of
         the Development Bank of Minas Gerais (Banco de Desenvolvimento de Minus Gerais -
         BDMG),of the Sanitation Company of Minas Gerais (Companhiade Saneamento de Minus
         Gerais - COPASA),and representatives from the relevant economic sectors. The network
         does not create a hierarchical link and it i s of great importance to the success of the
         program as it is through the network that the culture of PPP is disseminated and that the
         concepts and methodologies that are necessary for project implementation are consolidated.
         The PPP Program also counts on direct involvement of the State's General Auditing
         Service (Auditoria Geral do Estudo),the Advocacia Geral do Estado and the Company for
         the Economic Development of Minas Gerais (Companhiade Desenvolvimento EconBmico
         de Minus Gerais   - CODEMIG). The participation of all of these agents will be of great
         worth for the governance of the regulation and fiscalization structures.


The government of Minas Gerais will count on an operations manual so as to define the procedures
as per the interaction and operation of the PPP Management Council, the PPP Unit and the PPP
Network. This manual will state the steps that must be followed in all phases of project study and
elaboration in such a way as to strive for the best manner through which to develop knowledge and
make the PPPs viable. In addition to defining the role of each organization involved and the steps
to be followed, the manual's objective is to ensure that the knowledge acquired by means of each
project i s always usedto improve the remaining projects.

GuaranteesinPPPContractsinMinasGerais

As previously mentioned, the PPPs inBrazil should offer private investors a guaranteeincase there
are any flaws in payment on behalf of the contracting governmental party. Inthe case of Minas
Gerais, the use of various tools for the concession of guarantees i s foreseen. Such tools compose
the State's Arrangement for Guarantees (Arranjo de Garantias do Estudo). Among such tools let
us highlight the Fund for Public-Private Partnerships (Fundo de Parcerius Pu'blico-Privadas),
which was created by Law 14.869 of December 16, 2003. The financial agent for this fund i s the
BDMGandits managing organization is the SEDE.

The PPP fund will be composed of assets of various types and will offer great security to investors.
The following components are among the ones currently being evaluated:

-   Preferential nominative shares of the Electricity Company of Minas Gerais (Companhia
   Energe`ticade Minus Gerais- CEMIG);
-   Royalties paidby the CBMM to CODEMIG, as a result of niobium mining;



                                                                                                    99

-   Resourced loaned by the state of Minas Gerais from multilateral agencies so as to form assets
    and/or real guarantees;
-   Rightsover part of the dividends paidby CEMIG to the state of Minas Gerais;


Other possible tools include: contracting of insurance, the cession of credit and the association of
revenue resources. Notwithstanding, the Company for the Economic Development of Minas Gerais
will also play an important role as in addition to acting as the contracting party in PPP projects, it
can also make guaranteesto contracts available basedon its portfolio of assets.

The function of this ensuring structure supported by real assets is to offer security to investors. In
case a future government does not abide to its obligations, the investor i s automatically refunded by
means of the guarantee mechanisms foreseen in that contract. Thus, the investor that has running
and capital expenses to cover in the project is ensured in case of legal wrangles with the
government that can last for years.

The fund's composition and structure will be studied by a specific consultancy service renderedby
banks that have vast experience with long-term operations. It is probable that each of the fund's
components has a specific molding and different applicationfor each contract.

An interestingimplication of this structure created inMinas is that the Arrangement of Guarantees
will strive to avoid the issuingof precatory letters in case the state does not fulfill its obligation and
will, therefore, not contribute to increasing the indebtedness of the state.

The Selection of Projects and the FirstFive Piloting Projects

The government of Minas Gerais made the study of the molding of five piloting projects a priority
so as to begin the PPP Program. Inaddition to being important projects for the state, the projects
were chosen so as to represent different sectors. Therefore, efforts were made to maximize the
learning process from the new modality that was created.

Another care the government is taking regards the viability of the projects to be carried out. In
order to know if it i s worth taking a given project forward, all of its costs and benefits over time
should be considered. In order to make these estimates, the government i s preparing a matrix for
the selection of PPP projects.       This matrix contains the methodologies and criteria that are
necessary for their evaluation.

The five piloting projects that represent the beginningof the PPPprogram in Minas Gerais are:

    0    Recovery and enlargement of the infrastructure of highway MG-050 (Mateus Leme - SBo
         SebastiBo do Paraiso);

    0    Provision of 3000 new prison openings (including the services for the construction and
         operations of the units);

    0    Rendering basic sanitation services in municipalities that have low indexes of human
         development;

    0    Construction and operation of the State Government's Administrative Center in Belo
         Horizonte;

    0    Construction and operation of the University of Minas Gerais campus in Belo Horizonte.



                                                                                                      100

For 2006, studies as beingmade as per the possibility of including the modelingfor the expressway
from downtown Belo Horizonteto the Tancredo Neves International Airport.

For the molding of the first piloting projects, the government has been counting on services
rendered by specialized consulting firms that have great international experience with PPPs. It i s
expected that by means of these projects the knowledge and practices that are needed for new
partnerships will be consolidated and made appropriate, and will thus yield an important instrument
with which the economical and social challenges of Minas Gerais can be overcome.

The expectation i s that the MG-050 highway project and the prison openings project be the first
PPPs to be procured inMinas Gerais.

                              ANNEX 7: FISCALADJUSTMENT

A) Thefiscal adjustment effort of Minas Gerais, 2003-2005

Since 2003, Minas Gerais has adopted a strong fiscal adjustment policy which allowed an
impressive turnaround in its fiscal situation. The primary balance increased from 3.7% of net
current revenue in 2002 to 7.5% of net current revenue in 2003 and to 15.5% of net current revenue
in 2004. Current balance increasedfrom -5% of net current revenueto 2.8% in2003 andto 14%of
net current revenue in 2004. Total balance also grew from -12% of net current revenue in 2002 to -
6.5% in 2003 and to 2.4% of net current revenue in 2004. In2005, the figures for the first semester
of 2005 indicate the continuity and strengthening of the fiscal adjustment effort.

                           Figure 8: Minas Gerais: Fiscal Balances, 2000-04
                                     (% of Net Current Revenue)


           2 0 %
            1 5 %
            1 0 %
       g
       z      5 %
       E      D 74
            - 5 %
          -10YO
          -15 %




The sound fiscal performance of Minas Gerais was recognized by the National Treasury Secretary
(STN) through the approval of the Fiscal Adjustment Program for the period 2003-2006 and its
subsequentrenewal for the period 2005-2007 as agreedto in the debt agreement signed by the state
government and the STNunder the law 9496/97. Also, the state was upgraded in the STNranking
system on repayment capacity, going from C to B grade which allows the state to contract new
credit operations. Finally, the state recovered STN certification as the state i s regularly honoring
its debt service payments with the federal government.

The fiscal turnaround was obtained by a combination of revenue increases and a strict control of
current expenditures. Given the economic stagnation of 2003, tax revenues did not grow in 2003.
The recovery of the economic activity in 2004 and the improvement in the efficiency of tax
collection promoted a tax revenue increase of 12.4% in 2004.

B) Improvement of the tax collection performance and the modernization of the State Revenue
Service (SRE)

A good part of revenue increase in 2004 can be attributed to improvements in the tax collection
effort. Among the state government's thirty-one priority structural projects under the name of
"Geraes Programs", the modernization of the State Revenue Service (SRE) contributed for the
strong increase in state tax revenues. The implementation of a set of actions for the strengthening
of control to reduce tax evasion, the use of electronic tools to increase the efficiency of tax



                                                                                                 103

collection, the rationalization of processes and programs of fiscal-tax education were all
instrumentalin providing good results.

On the reduction of tax evasion, the state government implemented a matrix system for the state
VAT (ICMS) collection. Crossing information on tax collection by economic sectors and by
regions and comparing revenue performances among them, this systemallowed the identification of
potential tax evasion. The matrix management system also served as a basis for the definition of
tax revenue collection targets that are used in the result agreement contract signed by the SRE and
the Secretary of Planning and Management (SEPLAG). Furthermore, the SRE established a
scheme of incentives based on annual collection targets for SRE staff, derived from the result
agreement contract and the matrix control of revenue collection.

Under the modernization of SRE project, the state government launched an aggressive program to
enhance the efficiency of tax collection. Besides the tax collection growth objective, investments
in software and the modernization of administrative processes were directed to improve and
simplify the transactions between taxpayers and the StateFinance Secretary (SEF), which also have
positive effects on tax revenue.

The Integrated System of Administration of the State Revenue Service (SIARE) consists of the
electronic integration of all the administrative processes associated with the state taxes collection
activities. The SIARE has two main components. The first is the PROMAT system, which
consists in the standardization and the introduction of electronic devices in the transactions
between taxpayers and the SRE. The second is the CRIAR, which will electronically manage the
revenue system.

The PROMAT has two main dimensions: the taxpayer registration and information system and the
tax collection management system. Duringthe first phase of implementation in 2004, the modules
for taxpayer registration, alteration of registries and the emission of regularity certification for
taxpayers were incorporated into the taxpayer registration system. The issuance of tax collection
documents, the on-line Real State Transfers Tax (ITCD) collection, and the establishment of the
electronic system for the simplified collection of the ICMS for small firms (SIMPLES) were
integrated into the tax collection dimension of the PROMAT.

In 2005, seven additional modules are being integrated into the two dimensions of the PROMAT
system. On the taxpayer registration and information system, the fiscal account of taxpayers and
the taxpayer dossier modules are being tested and expected to be functioning at the end of the year.
On the tax collection dimension, the taxpayers' tax debvcredit system, the special regime of control
and supervision, the authorized fiscal document control, the automatic issuance of tax receipts for
small firms and autonomous producers, and the module of electronic data management are
expected to be implantedby mid2006.

The CRIAR development involves activities on the standardization of tax credit management
procedures, capacity enhancement activities for the SRE staff on tax credit claims by taxpayers,
elimination of tax credit duplicity and the decentralization of tax collection. It is expected that the
modules of the CRIAR system will be installed during 2006. The complete implementation of the
CRIAR will allow its integration with the PROMATinto the SIARE system.




                                                                                                   104

   Box 5: A Result-oriented Management Model for Tax Collection

   The impressive results in tax revenue collection can be explained by the introduction of a result-oriented
    management model within the State Revenue Sub-secretariat (SRE). In 2003, the State Secretariat of
   Finance (SFE) introduced for the first time a model based on results with the establishment of a working
    agreement with the SRE for tax collection to be developed in 2004. The SRE replicated this agreement
    with its central and regional units.

   In a more systematic way, in August 2004, the SRE signed a Result Agreement (RA) contract with the
    SFE and the SEPLAG which sets the performance results of the SRE in terms of state tax revenue
   collection for 2005. The RA has two main objectives: i)performance indicators and collection targets
   and ii)action plans and budgetary allocations to the SRE for the improvement of tax collection efficiency.

   The RA has three parties (SRE, SFE and SEPLAG): the SRE, the SFE and the SEPLAG. The obligations
   of the SRE include achievement of the results agreed, use of the resources allocated to the different
   activities included in the result agreement and production of regular reports to be sent to the Committee
   of Monitoring and Evaluation. The obligations of the SFE include monitoring of the execution of the RA,
   provision of budgetary and financial resources and guarantee of managerial autonomy to the SRE, and
   publication of the reports on the achievements of the targets. The obligations of the SEPLAG the
   provision of the budgetary resources to the SRE, guarantee of managerial autonomy, and approval of the
   RA reports and potential modifications to the original RA. The RA establishes a Committee of
   Monitoring and Evaluation, which will be composed by representatives of the three counterparts and a
   representative    from the     SRE    staff.   (Detailed information can be found in the site:
   http://www.sepla~.m~.~ov.br/~overno/clio~ue/acordo     resultado)

   The performance indicators and targets are divided in three main areas: i)tax collection of ICMS (state
   VAT); ii) tax collection of ITCD, IPVA and other user charges and other activities as tax debt recovery,
   administrative collection of tax credits; and (iii)organization of tax education events. The targets are
   defined quarterly with different weights (70% for the first area, 10% for the second and 10% for the
   third). Each target has a minimum, a superior, and an ideal level with ranks calculated by formula.

   The RA also includes an action and an improvement plan setting 20 actions that will enhancethe tax
   collection efficiency of the SRE. This part establishescompletion dates of the actions defined inboth
   plans with an overall weight of 10%. The RA also contains an annex that describes the methodology of
   monitoring and evaluation. Finally, the RA includes a detailed budget allocation of the activities included
   inthe action and improvementplans.

The integration of these modules guarantees the consistency of taxpayer data basis reducing the
space for tax evasion and the automatic issuance of tax certification and tax payments which will
reduce administrative costs not only for the SRE but mainly for the taxpayers. At the same time,
the system will allow an automatic integration with other state systems, as well as the revenue
services of the federal and municipal governments. This has potential impact on tax revenue
efficiency for the three levels of government.           The integration of the revenue with the state
financial management system (SIAFI) deserves particular attention as it will permit a better cash
flow administration and a more efficient financial execution.

C)Expenditure containment:personnel and operating expenditures

On the expenditure side, the government has exerted a strict control on current expenditures. In
2003 the government reduced expenditures by 7% while the recovery of revenues allowed an
increase of expenditures of 3% in 2004. Inparticular, the government promoted a strong reduction
on personnel expenditures of 10% in 2003 with a recovery of 5% in 2004. From 2002 to 2004
personnel expenditures were reduced by 2.9%. As net current revenues increased by 8.2% from
2002 to 2004, the state reduced the Fiscal Responsibility Law indicator of personnel expenditure on


                                                                                                           105

net current expenditures from 71% in 2002 to 61% in 2004, thus meeting the Fiscal Responsibility
Law requirement on this expenditure category.            Decomposing the effects, the reduction of
personnel expenditure was responsible for 30% of the reduction of the personnel expenditure to net
current revenue ratio while the revenue increase was responsible for 70% of this reduction.

The fall in personnel expenditures was the result of both short-term emergency actions as well and
long term structural actions. Among the first, the centralization of the payroll bill at the SEPLAG
secretary, the elimination of the upostilumento and of more than 1,300 commissioned positions, the
increase in the state employees contribution for the social security rate from 8% to 11% and the
establishment of a salary ceiling for all the state public sector. The centralization of the payroll bill
improved the control of personnel payments. Crossing information among the different personnel
databases of the state secretaries and with other data sets allowed the identification of irregular
payments and social security benefits.

At the same time, the new administration quickly got the constitutional approval of its
administrative reform proposal, with the reduction of the number of secretaries from 21 to 15, the
reduction of high top positions, and the change in the methodology for salary adjustment with the
replacement of time of services automatic increases by one based on individual performance. It
was estimated that the monthly nominal inertial growth was around 0.3% in the beginning of 2003,
and now should be around 0.15%, according to state officials. Also with the aim of reducing
personnel expenditure, there was the creation of a flexible timing of work ("bunco de horus") to
reduce additionalpayments for overtime ("horus extras").

It worth noticing that social security imbalance is also an important source of risk for personnel
expenditures.     The Minas Gerais state government social security system for government
employees i s composed of two funds: the FUNPENG (Fundo de PrevidZncia do Sewidor Pdblico
de Minus Geruis) and the FUNFIP(Fundo Finunceiro de Previd2nciu). The first one corresponds
to the state employees contracted after 2002. Given the lack of beneficiaries, this fund is in
equilibrium. The second one generates an annual deficit of about R$3 billion which is financed by
the state treasury. The actuarial deficit of FUNFIP is estimated at R$ 51.2 billion. Given this, an
increase in the future level of personnel expenditures (contributions to social security or benefits to
retiredpersonnel and pensioners) i s very likely.

The state government is taking a set of measures to alleviate the pressure of the social security
system obligations in the state accounts. In particular, the implementation of the public sector
employees social security reform, established in the Constitutional Amendment n. 41from 2003,
would allow the reduction of the actuarial disequilibria. Inthe short run, the reform establishes the
possibility of collection of social security contributions charged over retirement and pension
benefits, but with a floor of benefits (do you mean ceiling no it i s a floor, a minimum level,
beneficiaries that receive a transfer higher than R$ 2400 should pay the contribution?). This floor
i s the same for federal, state and municipal governments. This represented an advance to the
federal government, which had been trying to charge this contribution without success, but, for
state governments the gain i s not significant as the level of benefits is lower than the observed at
the federal government.

The state government is analyzing additional measures. The establishment of a complementary
social security systemwould allow the adoption of a general benefit ceiling. Managerial reforms as
the unification of the administration of the social security system for the three branches of
government would generate savings.



                                                                                                     106

The second most important component of current expenditure corresponds to the operating
expenditures. The adjustment in this expenditure category was impressive. From 2002 to 2004,
operating expenditures fell by 17% (7% in 2003 and 11% in 2004).

Besides the fiscal adjustment effort, the fall on operating expenditures also reflects the adoption of
a series of measures aimed at improving the public spending control systems. A new system of
services and goods administration i s being used since January 2004 (SIAD - Sistema de
Administra@io de Materiais e SewiCos do Estado de Minus Gerais). The coverage of the system
was expanded quickly. In 2004 90 percent of government purchaseswere processedby the SIAD
system through 2000 auctions for estimated savings of 18%.

This system has 15 modules that monitor the entire cycle of requirement, procurement, purchase,
distribution and consumption of materials and services allowing the control of the complete
contracting process of goods and services and the regulation of the price register system. The
incorporation of the modules i s progressive and it i s expected to complete the SIAD in the next
months. The system is being integrated to the Treasury information systems, mainly with the
SIAFIsystem.

The strengthening of government web systems is another relevant area not only for potential fiscal
gains but, mainly for the rationalization of the use of state resources. The implementation of the
electronic government initiative will make available state information through government
websites.




                                                                                                  107

                        ANNEX 8: PUBLIC SECTORMANAGEMENT

"Choque de Gestiio": State Reforminthe State of MinasGerais, 2003-05

During the tenure of the current Governor ACcio Neves, the State of Minas Gerais (MG) has
become nationally known for its aggressive state reform initiative. Under a strategic umbrella,
popularly known as "Choque de Cest6o (Management Shock)," the State Government has adopted
a series of legal, administrative and structural changes to the public administration in order to
"restructure the public machinery" (Le., reestablish fiscal equilibriumand improve performance of
the public administration). While the Minas program is not the only recent effort at public sector
reform in the Brazilian federation, the magnitude of challenge faced by the Government at the
beginning of its term and the audacity with which it has addressed these challenges place MG
among the most notable cases of comprehensive state reforminthe contemporary Brazil.

Initial Diagnosis: Fiscallyunsustainableand operationallyinefficient

The unsustainable public finances were the clearest and the most worrisome sign of MG's
institutionaldysfunction in the early 2000s. Inparticular, personnel expenditures surpassed 70% of
net current revenue, well above the permitted threshold of 60% as established in the Law of Fiscal
Responsibility.   Inaddition, a comprehensive diagnosis of MG's policy challenges, which was
prepared by the Minas Gerais Development Bank (BDMG), noted other weaknesses in MG's
public administration, including:


    0    Fragmented administrative structure as a result of years of uncoordinated institutional
         creations (e.g., the administrative structure of the agriculture sector, which might have been
         adequate inthe 1970~-80s,did not reflect the increasedrole of the private sector)

    0    Inflexible human resource management that causes inefficient deployment of public
         servants (e.g., in the education sector, teachers used to be hired into very specific jobs and
         locations, which made it virtually impossible to re-assign them from one school to another,
         let alone from one municipality to another; nearly 2,000 teachers were working outside the
         classrooms due to the reduced student enrollment)

    0    Ineffective salary policy that cannot be used to motivate and retain specialized staff (e.g.,
         the Government has had a policy of permitting into the public service graduates of the
         government-run School of Government, but a number of these graduates would leave the
         public service after a few years given the inhospitable working conditions in the public
         sector)

    0    Weak planning system (e.g., government planning could not ensure that priority objectives
         would guide government activities, and instead, availability of cash resources and political
         urgency dictated resource allocations)

    0    Delayed development of e-government initiatives (compared to the federal government and
         some states)




                                                                                                   108

MeasuresAdopted

Administrative Reform and WageBill Controls

In light of these diagnoses, the Government took decisive measures to implement a comprehensive
public sector reform upon assuming power in January 2003. A first set of measures concentrated
on adjusting the personnel establishment, regaining fiscal sustainability of the wage bill, and
reorganizing the State Government's macro structure ("administrative reform") to make it leaner
and more consistent with the redefined role of the state, with an emphasis on revamped policy
planning and inter-sectorial coordination.      Using a series of legal measures, the Government
merged organizational units. These mergers resulted in elimination of 1,326 political appointee
positions (and the corresponding salary and benefit expenditures), or about 20% of all such
positions in the public sector. According to the Government, this measure alone produced financial
saving of R$19.8 million. Other measures taken to control personnel expenditures included:


     0    Upward adjustment of public servants' retirement contributions from 8% to 11% of their
          base salary;

     0    Changing the criteria for calculating non-salary benefits (Le,, top-up) from length of
          service to a performance-basedbonus;

     0    Elimination of the rule that granted former holders of political appointments the same
          salary and benefit packageeven after they vacate these appointments (apostilamento);

     0     Reduction of salaries of political appointees and definition of the Governor's salary
          (R$10,500) as the ceiling for the entire public sector;

     0    Better control of staff attendance and part-time working arrangements (via Banco de
          Horas).


To ensure that the financial gains achieved through these measures are not easily reversed by
imprudent future decisions, the Government has mandated the cabinet-level committee (Cdrnarade
CoordenaGGo Geral, Planejamento e Gestzo, CCGPG) to review and approve all policy decisions
with fiscal implications, including sectors' requests for new hires and other personnel or
administrative decisions. Upon receiving requests, the Secretariat of Planning and Management
(SEPLAG) analyzes the medium-term fiscal implications and recommends an action to the
CCGPG.        SEPLAG has centralized management of payrolls, including of the Indirect
Administration entities (e.g., public enterprises), to gain full control over salary payments and
standardize criteria for concession of benefits to public servants. In order to identify irregular
concessions of benefits (including retirement benefits), SEPLAG is also conducting audits of
individual public servants' records, although this task is proving difficult to implement given the
sheer volume involved - currently there are around 4,000 cases of retirement requests that are
overdue.

Centralizing decisions for strategic establishment control at the highest instance i s a positive step
toward responsible fiscal management of the personnel contingent. However, without adequate
information, the cabinet committee would not be able to make the most informed decisions. The
State i s therefore working to improve its integrated personnel data system (SISAP). Some of the
SISAP modules are not fully operational yet, but the Government i s working toward the system's
full operationalization during 2006.




                                                                                                  109

Human Resource Policy Reforms

Establishing quantitative control over the wage bill was necessary for regaining fiscal
sustainability, but hardly sufficient to improve the performance of the state bureaucracy. To
achieve the latter, the State Government has elaborated a new, more coherent policy to manage
human resources and strengthen the merit features of public administration. The main pillars are:
(i)newpublicsectorcareerstructure; and(ii)newmechanismsfor stimulatingincentivesand
    a
accountability of individual public servants.

New career structure: In the Brazilian administrative tradition, a proven way to fortify the merit
principle is to structure well-designed careers within given administrative or sectorial functions.
Thus, the federal government has managed to upgrade the quality of its staff in key areas of
economic management (via careers of economists, financial analysts, planning and budget anaiysts,
tax administrators, etc.), prosecution (public ministry), and a few other areas.          The Minas
government is following this approach, and has restructured its career system, not only with a view
to developing merit-based human resource structures, but also to increase flexibility in strategic
management of human resources. The previous structure where the public sector jobs were
classified into 893 detailed classes (and their sub-divisions) was transformed into a less rigid
structure composed of 132 careers divided into 14 main job groups (e.g., management, planning,
treasury, audit and political-institutional group, environment group, basic education group, etc.). In
the previous system, a public servant recruited into a particular class of job could not be re-
assigned to other jobs (which severely limited the government's ability to re-allocate its human
resources according to the changing needs and priorities), nor could he/shebe promotedbeyond the
upper boundary established for each class into which he/she was recruited. The new structure not
only allows the government greater flexibility in staff re-deployment, but also allows well-
performing public servants to be promoted within their vertical career structures so long as they
meet certain criteria (e.g., good performance, experience, additional education/training).

Performance bonus schemes and individual performance evaluations: Another pillar of the
merit-orientedpersonnel managementreform i s the introduction of performance-oriented incentive
schemes. These measures are also linked to the broader efforts at results-based management
(discussed below).     The most basic form of these incentive schemes i s called Adicional de
Desempenho, ADE (or performance bonus in rough English translation). To introduce the ADE,
the Government had to replace the old form of "bonuses" given strictly on the basis of length of
service (irrespective of the pubic servants' performance at their jobs). The measure required an
amendment to the State Constitution, which was approved in July 2003. The new rule applies
automatically to those public servants who have been appointed since this date (11,321 appointees
as of August 2005). The remaining public servants were given the options of staying within the old
system or switching to the new rule. (According to the government official, no one has opted out
of the old rule.)

With ADE public servants may earn a bonus of up to 70% of their basic salaries, as determined by
their individual performance (50% weight), their training  (lo%), and the performance of the agency
in which they work (40%).        Those public servants whose agencies do not participate in the
institutional performance evaluations (see below) are not entitled to that 40% share in the ADE
scheme.

The Government has taken care to ensure that these monetary incentives do not affect sustainability
of the wage bill. The state LDO states that the overall envelope for wage increases i s restricted to:
[annual change in ICMS revenue -crecimento vegetativo] x [a determined %I.


                                                                                                  110

The percentage in the formula i s set to keep the overall wage bill within the LRE limits. Now, the
wage bill envelope will be impacted by the new salary scale proposals that are currently
(September 2005) sitting in the state legislature for consideration. As monetary awards based upon
individual performance evaluations also count toward the total wage bill, the formula (with the
LRE) i s a cap on both salary scale increases and individual performance awards. Based upon the
estimated costs of the approved salary scales and an estimate of the number of employees eligible
for individual performance awards, the amount of money for individual performance awards will be
set. The first individual performance evaluation monetary awards are scheduled to be granted in
2006.

Individual performance evaluations are a cornerstone of Minas' results-oriented personnel
managementreform. Each public servant would agree ex ante with hidher superior the criteria and
goals for which hidher actual performance will be assessed. Poor performers would be identified
and directed to improve their capabilities through training, or dismissed from the public service in
extreme cases (two consecutive unsatisfactory performance ratings, three unsatisfactory ratings
within five years, or four within 10 years). Although international experiences show a number of
practical difficulties in institutionalizing individual performance evaluations in the public sector
such as the tendency to encourage staff to perform "to the numbers" (i.e., focusing almost
exclusively on those tasks that are explicitly linked to the performance indicators and neglecting
other, equally important tasks), or, more commonly among developing countries, the tendency of
managers to award positive performance ratings to most or all staff and thus for the performance
bonuses to become de facto entitlements which everyone receives irrespective of the actual
performance levels. The Minas government i s aware of these pitfalls, and its approach appears to
be coherent at least at the conceptual level. The new system i s being rolled out gradually (The
government has evaluated 14,000 public servants with the newly developed methodwithout linking
the results, as yet, to ADE or other incentive mechanisms.). It would be in the interest of the
government to monitor its effects rigorously as it i s applied over coming years.

Revitalization of the Planning Apparatus and Results-BasedManagement

Reforms of government planning have been "in vogue" in Brazil since the late 1990s, largely
thanks to the federal government's effort to revamp its own planning framework and link it to fiscal
realities, budgeting, and results-oriented management of public policy programs. A number of
states and municipalities have initiated similar efforts since then. The efforts thus far by the
Government of MGare arguably the most systematic and strategic.

Geraes: One of the hallmarks of Choque de GestGo in Minas i s the initiative called Geraes
(Gestcio Estratkgica dos Recursos e A@es do Estado, Strategic Management of Resources and
Activities of the State). The initiative revolves around 31 priority programs called "structural
projects" (projetos estruturadores, PES). Following the model developed by the federal
government, each of these 31structural projects has performance indicators, each i s led by a senior
project manager responsible for its performance and answerable directly to the Governor, and each
i s guaranteed budgetary and financial resources (the Law of Budget Guidelines or LDO prohibits
legislative amendments from reducing funding for these structural projects and the SEPLAG and
the Treasury guarantee not to retain spending authorizations for these projects, a common practice
in Brazil's public budget execution).       The Minas government's ability to guarantee funding
predictability is a notable political achievement which the federal government and other state
governments have so far not been able to accomplish.



                                                                                                111

Results agreements:      Another key difference between Minas' approach to the results-based
planning/management and the previous federal effort is the use of results agreements as explicit
instruments of accountability. The government initially intended to sign results agreements with
the manager of each of the 31 structural projects. Given the high transaction costs involved in
developing these agreements, with the legal status of a "contract," the government has adjusted its
approach and now has opted to sign results agreements with secretariats and other government
entities. Since the LDO prohibits changes to the budget allocations to the structural projects from
the executive proposal, the agencies in charge of implementingstructural projects can plan ahead
and continue preparing for budget execution (e.g., continuing with a procurement activity) at the
very beginning of the following year. Typically in Brazil, uncertainty about the exact budget
allocation and the expectation that a portion of the approved budget will be retained by the
Ministries of Planning and Finance keep agencies from continuing with program execution between
fiscal years. Thus, this arrangement has apparently contributed to increasedoperational efficiency
in executing the structural projects by providing them with greater budgetary predictability. Actual
implementation of the 31 structural projects is closely monitoredby SEPLAG with an information
system (SIGPlan usedby the federal government).

Once a results agreement i s signed at the institutional (i.e., agency) level, it becomes the basis for
institutional (agency) performance evaluations. The agency's performance i s tracked on a regular
timetable (Le. quarter, trimester, semester) depending on the nature of the activities. When an
agency achieves its pre-set performance targets while generating savings in its current expenditure
budget or an increase of own revenues, it i s allowed to redistribute part of the saving inthe form of
"productivity award" to its staff. Similar to individual performance evaluations, accumulation of
poor agency performance is subject to sanction such as cancellation of certain administrative
advantages (e.g. budget predictability, productivity award). Results agreements have been signed
with the following "structural projects" and government secretariatdagencies:

Structural Projects with Results Agreements Signed

     1. Pavimentagiio de LigagGes e Acessos Rodovicirios aos Municl`pios (Paving of Road
         Connections to Municipalities)
    2. GestiioAmbiental MG Skculo XXZ (Minas EnvironmentalManagement 21st Century)
    3. Minas sem Fome (Minas without Hunger)

Government Agencies with Results Agreements Signed

     1. IEF- InstitutoEstadual de Florestas (environment)
    2. IGAM- Instituto Mineiro de Gestiio de Aguas (water resource management)
    3. FEAM- Fundasgo Estadualdo Meio Ambiente (environment)
    4. HEMONINAS - Fundas20 Centro de Hematologia e Hemoterapia de Minas Gerais (health)
    5. IMA - Instituto Mineiro de Agropecuaria (agriculture and fishery)
    6. IPEM- Instituto de Pesos e Medidas do Estado de Minas Gerais (science and technology)
    7. AGE - Advocacia Geral do Estado de Minas Gerais (1egaVadministration)
    8. SEPLAG- Secretariat of Planning and Management (administration)
    9. SEF -Secretariat of Finance (administration)
     10. SES - Secretariat of Health (health)
     11. FUNED-Funda$io       EzequielDias (health)
     12. AUGE - Auditoria Geral da Uniiio (auditing)
     13. FCS -Fundasgo C16vis Salgado (culture)
    14. SEMAD -Secretariat of Environment and Sustainable Development (environment)


                                                                                                   112

    15. SEDS - Secretariat of Social Defense (public security)
    16. IPSEMG- Instituto de Previdencia dos Servidores do Estadode Minas Gerais
    17. VISA - Superintendencia de Seguranqa SanitBria

Contracting out service delivery: Reliance on results-basedmanagementtechniques is not limited
to performance compacts within the public sector. The government's desire to expand provision of
services within the state's limited fiscal capacity has led to the policies of partnerships with non-
governmental providers of services: through public-private partnerships (PPP), mostly in
infrastructure provision, and through OSCIPs (Orgunizu@o du Sociedade Civil de Interesse
Pziblico, Civil Society Organization with Public Interest) in social areas. Minas Gerais was among
the first in the Brazilian federation to pass a PPP Law. The Government has set up a specialized
unit within the Secretariat of Economic Development, and i s preparing its first PPP projects (in
roads, water and sanitation).

An OrganizupZodu Sociedude Civil de Interesse Pziblico (OSCIP) is a legal designation conferred
by the State on a non-profit organization with social objectives consistent with public policy goals.
The OSCIP is intended as an instrument to enable a new form of partnership between the state and
civil society (or the so-called "Terceiro Setor") in the delivery of public services, redefining
thereby the role of the state. The innovation of OSCIPs is that these institutions, representing
"organized civil society," can enter into partnerships with the state, receiving budget resources and
other public goods to support their activities.

The legal foundation of the OSCIP model in Minas Gerais is Lei 14.870/2003, as regulated by
Decree 43.749/2004 and Resolution 48. (The precursor to the Minas OSCIP model i s the federal
Lei 9.790/99.) These legal documents define the characteristics and procedures necessary for an
organization to qualify as an OSCIP, and the standards (e.g., accounting) that must be satisfied for
an OSCIP to enter into a Partnership Agreement (Term0 de Purceriu) with the state. [Note: certain
organizations are barred from becoming OSCIPs, for example commercial organizations, labor
unions, political party and religious organizations.] The Partnership Agreement must specify the
social objective of the OSCIP, and the responsibilities, rights and obligations of the signatories. It
also includes the goals to be achieved through the Agreement, and how those are to be measured.

The arguments for the creation of the OSCIP model are that they will lead to a more efficient
allocation of resources, more responsive to the needs of citizens, and a more effective and efficient
delivery of services. They are meant to induce greater civil society participation in implementing
public policy, subjecting public resources to greater social control, while also strengthening social
capital. OSCIPs are governed by private sector law, and therefore enjoy managementflexibility.

The states of CearB and Si20 Paulo have also begun experimenting with the OSCIP model,
particularly in the health sector. The government of Minas Gerais beganto certify organizations as
OSCIPs in 2004 (e.g., in education, environment, etc.). The Government has already qualified 26
non-governmental organizations as potential service providers as OSCIPs in areas ranging from
social assistance, health, and education/culture/sports to environment and to and social and
economic development in general. The government i s discussingsigningof "terms of partnership"
with several of them, and has already signed six Partnership Agreements.

Electronic Government: Systematic and extensive use of e-government tools i s one of the features
of the Minas government's approach to public management reform. The government created the
Executive Committee of the Electronic Government to establish a common focus among the e-
government initiatives. Composed of 2lDeputy-Secretaries, the Committee has the authority to set
standards for content and quality of information and services provided by Portal Minus, the
government website. The Electronic Governance Department from SEPLAG i s responsible for
implementation of Committee resolutions such as carrying on content evaluations and audit of each
agency's home page.




                                                                                                    114

Portal Minas was created in 2004 to be a door for government services. The concept was to
change organization of information from a formal (institutional) structure into a more user-friendly
one according to subject matters of interest to citizens (education, health) and types of services that
they seek. Another classification i s around "life events" that use more accessible language, like
"Getting you.driver's license", "Paying the IPVA" to make information search easier and faster.

The management of Portal Minas i s decentralized. Information and services are updated by each
agency based on the Committee guidelines. For instance, the agencies' websites must run in any
software, information requests (Faze Conosco) must be replied within 48 hours, and content must
be factually accurate. Electronic Governance Department does the oversight of agencies' sites to
check if the content is insufficient, intermediate or advanced in quality.

Several initiatives to improve government management, quality of services delivery and
transparency have been taken by Choque de Gest6o. Governance has improved with better use of
information instruments such as project monitoring systems and more user friendly management
reports.  There was a reduction of current costs, administrative personnel and time through
reengineering of processes like office automation, intranet, workflow and digital certification.
Additionally, the government has been offering information and services through terminals or
online, for instance emission of documents, bills, forms, payment of taxes and traffic tickets
(DetranNet). The structural project Digital Inclusion (Znclusik Digital) i s a program to promote
Internet access to the population of small municipalities. By the end of 2005, around 320 internet
centers will be installed in public spaces and 40 technology centers. Transparency of decisions has
been enhanced with a telephone line for governmental information (LIG-Minas) and openness of
procurement process with reverse auction (LicitaNet). Also, there i s information available for
entrepreneurs on sources of financing, export procedures and how to close business.

Procurement reform: The goal of improving efficiency and reducing government expenditures has
led a number of governments in the Brazilian federation, includingMinas, to focus on procurement
reform. The Minas government has initiated an aggressive use of "pregzo" (reverse auction) to
purchase standard supplies, developed a single registry of suppliers (including a registry of
suppliers barred from participating in public procurement), and adopted mandatory use of the
Integrated System of Administration of Materials and Services of the State (SIAD). With these
(and other) measures, the Government has reportedly obtained savings of 32 percent of the cost of
government purchases and procurement, totaling R$2 billion a year. The government plans to
extend the use of e-preg6o to further improve the economy in government procurement, and
complete a number of SIADmodules that are still not fully operational.




                                                                                                   115

                      ANNEX 9: PRIVATE SECTORDEVELOPMENT

Support of PrivateSector Developmentby the Governmentof Minas Gerais

The State Government of Minas Gerais has created an array of mechanisms and institutions with
the objective of promoting private sector development in the state in order to promote growth.
Most, but not all, of the government initiatives in support of private sector development are
included in some of the 31 structural projects (projetos estruturadores) initiated by the current
administration of Minas Gerais.

The overall approach to support private sector development in Minas Gerais i s to provide, through
the offer of improved channels of access between the state and the private sector, solutions to
facilitate the operation, expansion and modernization of established businesses, as well as the
implementation of new businesses in Minas Gerais, including areas such as tax, credit,
environmental regulations, infrastructure, and the registration of businesses.

The main components of the government strategy in support of private sector development in
Minas Gerais are: 1) The structural project of Competitive Business of Minas (which includes a
special line of credit and programs to lesser the impact of government bureaucracy in the private
sector: Facilita Minas and MinasFAcil); 2) Simples Minas (which is a simplified tax treatment for
small and medium-sized firms); 3) The Institute of Integrated Development of Minas Gerais (INDI,
which acts as the business promotion agency of the government); and 4) The Public-Private
Partnerships (in which Minas Gerais has taken a lead role in Brazil and it is expected to increase
substantially private sector investment in infrastructure). The first three are covered in this annex,
while the last one is described indetail inAnnex 7.

1)CompetitiveBusinessof Minas

The main component of this effort is summarized in the projeto estruturudor called Competitive
Business of Minas (Empresu Mineira Competitimu). As one of the 31 structural projects, this
program, led by the Banco de Desenvolvimento de Minas Gerais (Development Bank of Minas
Gerais) or BDMG, has two components, the first one, a credit line (Empresa Mineira Competitiva)
aimed at improving the competitiveness of small and medium-sized firms, and the second one,
Fucilitu Minas, is a program aimed at generating a business-friendly environment in Minas Gerais
so as to facilitate the generation of private investment, and make possible the success of businesses
by easing the sometimes complicated and bureaucratic relationship between the different state
institutions and the firm.

1.1)CreditLineEmpresa Mineira Competitiva

This line of credit for small and medium-sized firms, aims at financing the modernization of
processes and increases in competitiveness and productivity for the production of goods and
services. The line of credit includes basically intangibles (and not equipment per-se) such as the
development of products and processes, adaptation of programs and consulting services for
management, environmental management, training to improve research and development, quality
control and marketing, modernization of computer equipment and software, and others.




                                                                                                  116

1.2) Facilita Minus

The Program Fucilitu Minus was created in 2004 and i s under the leadership of the President of
BDMG. The main objective of the program i s to diminish the impact of the government
bureaucracy in the private sector, and simplifying the relationship between different levels of the
state government and the firms. Private sector investment can be fostered, according to the design
of this program, by easing transactions costs to firms and reducingbureaucratic redtape.

The program aims at promoting private investment in Minas Gerais by introducing administrative
reforms and technical coordination among the state government agencies so as to facilitate the
creation of new firms and the expansion of existing ones.

Facilita Minus has created a website in which it is possible, for current and potential investors, to
inquire about taxation, firm registration, credit lines, environmental regulations, and infrastructure.
A team of experts, provided by different government agencies, is in charge of analyzing and
designing optimal solutions to the different inquiries.

The first practical outcome of the Facilita Minas program, has been the creation of MinasFdcil, an
office in charge of minimizing the amount of effort and time to register a new business in Minas
Gerais

2) MinasF6cil

The design of MinasFdcil consists of the creation and staffing of an office in which the processes
of the different state institutions that deal with the registration of new firms are integrated. The
first office was to be inaugurated in September 2005 in the capital of the state, Belo Horizonte.
The guidingphilosophy of MinasFdcil is that firms should concentrate on its business development
plan: market demand, clients, suppliers, credit, technology, etc., while the government will try to
reduce to the minimumthe costs, interms of resources and time, to the new firm.

The process of MinasFdciZ starts with a preliminary inquiry so as to verify that there are no legal
impediments for the investor (future firm and its legal structure) to begin the process of opening a
business according to the regulations of the state, the federal government, and the local
government. This can be done either in person or through the Internet. Following this first step,
the investor can get an overall picture of what is needed in terms of processes and documents,
including the legal requirements of the different government agencies.           Once the office of
MinasFdcil answers positively in support of the registration of the new firm, MinasFBcil provides a
specific list of requisites to be presentedby the investor. The investor then presents all the required
documentation to MinasFdcil, following the responseto the initial inquiry.

In addition to concentrating all of the government agencies that are required in the process of
registering a new business in one place, as a one-stop shop, MinusFdcil's administrative process
has been designed so as to eliminate the need for duplicate documents, as they are all now part of a
single process. The implementation of this process of selection aims at helping both the investor
and the government, by avoiding extra work to the government agencies and giving to the investor
an overall picture of the process about all the government agencies included inthe registration of a
new firm.

The list of registries needed for opening a firm in Minas Gerais includes: Identity number of
registered firms (NIRE), the national registry of firms, or tax identification number (CNPJ), the


                                                                                                   117

municipal and state registries, and the license of location and operation. In addition, the process
includes environmental license, health licenses, and fire department license.

3) Simples Minas

The State Secretary of Finance devised a simplified tax treatment for small and medium-sized
enterprises. Simples Minus is defined as a program of simplified and differentiated treatment for
small and medium-sized enterprises. It was created by Law inJuly of 2004.

Inorder to benefit from Simples Minus, gross annual total sales of the firm should be less than
R$2.2 million. The simplifiedtax treatment allows firms to check the value added tax (ICMS) in a
more convenient way. Total income can be estimated as either "real income" (receitu brutu real)
or presumed income (receitu brutu presumidu). "Real income" i s equivalent to the sum of all the
sales of goods and services, as accounted by the documents of sale. This method applies mainly to
industries, or productive firms. Presumed income is estimated as the sum of all inputs used, and
accounted for receipts of sale, increased by a percentage estimated as the value added of the
economic activity of the firm. This method can be used by industries, but it is mandatory for
commercial firms.

The program simplifies the "formalization" of firms, by facilitating the registration on the internet
with almost no requirements. Taxes are exempt for annual revenue lower than R$5,600, and scale
i s created such that the tax-exemption i s reduced progressively as annual revenue increases. An
electronic system of tax preparation (SIAP) has been created with a simplified structure. Tax
credits will be maintained, even if the ICMS taxes collected are lower, up to 10 %, than the verified
tax declaration. Another advantage of SimplesMinus i s that it does not require the firms and
individuals to keep accounting books. Instead, all registers will be kept through the Internet in the
Secretary of Finance.




                                                                                                 118

4) The Institute of Integrated Development of Minas Gerais (INDI)

INDI(Instituto de Desenvolvimento Integrado de Minas Geruis) was reformed in July of 2005 on
the basis of the Institute of Industrial Development of Minas Gerais. INDI was created as a
privately managed institution, owned by the Development Bank of Minas Gerais (BMDG) and the
Power Company of Minas Gerais (CEMIG), both state-owned companies. The board of directors
of INDI is composed of the State Secretaries of Economic Development, Planning and
Management, Finance, and the Presidents of BDMGand of CEMIG.

The main objective of INDI i s the promotion of private investment in the state of Minas Gerais.
The concept behind INDIis that of a business promotion agency, but with greater autonomy and
political weight, as it can more easily influence required changes within the government agencies,
as they are leadingit.

According to the Board of Directors, INDI, as an agency in charge of promotinginvestment, will:

    Keep up-to-date systems and data as to monitor business projects and investments within the
    state.
    To organize and lead the efforts of other government agencies in order to promote investment
    and strengthen private sector firms.
    Articulate strategies with municipalities, government agencies, and local communities to
    promote regionaldevelopment.
    Promote with specific actions and extensive campaigns, products and services of firms as well
    as the potential of Minas Gerais for business development.
    Coordinate the participation of Minas Gerais in an effective and intensive way, in fairs and
    business meetings at the national and national level.

Even before its recent reorganization, INDI has played a significant role in business promotion.
From 1972 to mid-2005, INDIassistedmore than 1,600 investment projects, with a total investment
of about US$16 billion and more than 280,000 jobs generated. By June 2005, INDIwas working
with more than 200 projects with a potential investment of US$8.7 billion, of which US$2.7 billion
have been or are on the process of being implemented.




                                                                                              119

Box 6: Administrative unitsof INDI

         a) Unit for Regional and Economic Assessments: In charge of statistics, technical assessments,
economic analysis, analysis of regional development poles, strategic information, keeping up-to-date
information of incentives given by the state for new investments, permanent actualization and promotion of tax
and fiscal legislation in Minas Gerais, evaluation of infrastructure in the different regions of the state.

         b) Unit for Strategic Information: In charge of updating a database, management of business
contacts, data collection in relation to public and private investment in Minas Gerais promoted by the state
government, monitoring of projects and investments, monitoring of obstacles and/or difficulties faced by
current and potential investors, and collection and promotion at the national and international level of results
obtained by the development system of the state.

         c) Unit for Institutional Promotion of Minas Gerais: Incharge of the organization of Minas Gerais in
national and international business events and fairs, promotion of the state, state products, and business
opportunities - "Minas Brand" (Marca Minas), leading campaign of the state advertising agencies in relation
to the promotion of investment, organization of business meetings in key cities of the state, with the
participation of domestic and international firms, organization of road-shows, workshops and other forums in
Brazil and abroad, active involvement with chambers of commerce of other countries, support to firms from
Minas Gerais in the external market.

         d) Unit for Regional Integration and Support to Firms: Creation and support of a registry of firms
and output from Minas Gerais, integration with municipalities and other entities of micro-regions, program to
intensify the sale of products and services of the state by foreign firms in the state, support of firms under
stress by helping them to link with other firms, an active program to promote exports of state firms, programs
to promote the gains in competitiveness, productivity and quality developed by firms within the state.

         e) Unit for Investment and Business: Incharge of attracting investment in the industrial, commercial
and services sectors, promote measures to stimulate the establishment of firms as suppliers of other firms,
provide managerial support to new projects to be established andlor expanded in the state, provide up-to-date
information for an area of new projects, and maintain a stock of projects to be offered to potential investors.
