           ANNEX 10: RELATIONSHIPTO OTHERBANKOPERATIONS

This Annex describes the ongoing and planned support by the World Bank Group to the State of
Minas Gerais.

a) Other World BankLoansto the State of MinasGerais

Rural Poverty Reduction Project. The Bank i s currently negotiating a US$35 million dollar loan
supporting community-driven rural development (PCPR: Projeto de Combate h Pobreza Rural).
Resources will focus on productive subprojects in the three poorest areas inthe north of Minas: the
Jequitinhonha and Mucuri Valleys, and the Norte de Minas. Given the extreme inter-regional
inequality within Minas, the PCPR would complement the Partnership for Development, with the
former focusing explicitly on regional inequality, the latter on the overall climate for sustainable
growth and social progress.

Cancelled State Privatization Loan. The Bank's Board approved a State Privatization Loan for
Minas Gerais in 1998 (Staff Appraisal Report No. 16466-BR). The objective of this investment
loan was to support the state's privatization and concession program, reducing vulnerabilities to
losses on banking operations and increasing the efficiency of gas and highway maintenance
services. The project also included social sector grants to mitigate the social costs of adjustment,
and road and school maintenance and rehabilitation. The components of this project were (i)
privatization of state banks (Banco de Crkdito Real de Minas Gerais and Banco de Estado de
Minas Gerais); (ii) the salelconcession of Companhia Estadual de Gris de Minas Gerais; (iii) the
concession of 460 km of state roads; (iv) an improved regulatory framework for the private
provision of public services; and (v) fiscal performance consistent with the capital spending
program and agreed fiscal indicators. Despite its approval by the World Bank's Boardof Directors
and Brazil's National Treasury, the state government, elected in 1998, declined the loan.

b) FederalOperations

Roads. The Federal Highway Decentralization and Rehabilitation Project provides financing for
the maintenance and rehabilitation of about 800 kmof roads on the MG state portions of the federal
paved road network, the backbone of Brazil's transportation system. As this i s a project executed
by the federal government, the participation of the state government is limited to participating to
the design and supervision of the works.

Health.    Municipalities with populations of over 100,000 participate in the Family Health
Extension Project. The state is also the recipient of loan proceeds to strengthen M&E of family
health services. The state as well as 3-4 urban municipalities in the metropolitan area of Belo
Horizonte will also be recipients of financing through VIGISUS 11(recently declared effective).
The Bank has an active technical dialogue with the State Secretariat of Health.

Environment. The Bank supports several NGOs (e.g., Funda@o Biodiversitas) and Universities
(UFMG, UFUberl2ndia) in Minas Gerais through grants from the PROBIO and FUNBIO Projects.
These grants tend to be small in size (< $100,000), but have played an important role in
strengthening conservation efforts for remnant Atlantic Forest and Cerrado throughout the State.
These activities have kept the Bank engaged with key stakeholders in the state's environmental
management and are complementary to the support proposed in the operation for improved
environmentallicensing through automation and decentralization.



                                                                                                121

Federal level DPL. The proposed operation also ties in with two series of programmatic DPL at
the federal level: the Fiscal Reform series of loans reinforcing fiscal balance, the most recent of
which supported social security reform,63 and the series for Sustainable and Equitable Growth,
which supports microeconomic growth-oriented reforms at the national

c) MunicipalLending

Minas Gerais has been the pioneer of World Bank municipal lending in Brazil. The Bank's
objective is a coherent long-term strategy for Bank lending to municipal governments in Brazil,
recognizing the important role these governments have to play in providing basic services to the
population, in particular the poor. The program is being developed in response to a growing
demand by municipal governments to borrow from the World Bank.               To date, the federal
government has authorized 15 municipalities to seek World Bank financing, with a federal
guarantee, of which three are in Minas Gerais. While these operations deal directly with the
municipal governments, the state water company (COPASA) has a role to play in complementary
investments in Water Supply and Sanitation.

Betim. The World Bank's first loan to a municipality has been developed with Betim, a medium-
sized city near Belo Horizonte. The objectives of the project are: (a) to promote sustainable socio-
environmental development; (b) to reduce inequality; and (c) to enhance the city's quality of life
through integrated, well-targeted investments in local infrastructure and social services, coupled
with broader institutional strengthening to improve municipal governance and regulatory policy.
Similar loans are in their final phase of preparation in Belo Horizonte, the state capital, and
Uberaba.

d) Grants

Minas benefits from two sources of grant funding administered by the World Bank. First, in one
slum area of the state capital Belo Horizonte, the anti-violence programFica Vivo is supported by
Bank technical assistance through a Dutch trust fund. Fica Vivo is viewed as best practice in
community-driven violence reduction programs, and i s included among the state government's 31
priority structural projects.

Plantar. The prototype carbon fund i s financing a carbon offset credit to Plantar SA, a
manufacturer of pig iron in four areas of Minas Gerais within 200 km of Belo Horizonte. The
purchase aims to achieve reductions in carbon dioxide emissions of 12 million tons over the
lifetime of the project (28 years). These reductions will be achieved through establishing new fuel
wood plantations, switching from coking coal to charcoal, and regenerating native forests on
pasture land. The prototypefund will purchase US$13.8 incarbon emissions reductions.

e) IFC Operations

IFC has investments in the following companies in Minas Gerais: Algar Telecom, Andrade
Gutierrez, Coteminas, Fosfkrtil, Guilman Amorin (hydro plant), Mineraqdes Brasileiras Reunidas
(MBR), Samarco, and Wembley. Its latest investments have been in Satipel (US$25 million) and
V&M do B r a d (the Netherlands Carbon Facility has committed 15m to purchase carbon dioxide
emission reductions from V&M).        IFC grant funding supports the Zmtituto Terra (technical

assistance for environmentally and socially sustainable business in Aimores) and Voluntdrios de
Minus (a FIEMG corporate social responsibility project).      The IFC has participated in project
identification and expressed interest in seeking ways to support PPPcontracts.
